 = Musician, singer-songwriter, radio show host\n| instruments     = [[Mandolin]], [[bouzouki]], [[mandola]], [[banjo]], [[guitar]], [[tenor guitar]], [[drums]], [[sitar]], [[piano]], [[violin]], [[viola]], [[cello]], [[double bass]], [[vocals]]\n| years_active    = 1989\u2013present\n| label           = {{Plainlist|\n* [[Sugar Hill Records (bluegrass)|Sugar Hill]]\n* [[Nonesuch Records|Nonesuch]]\n}}\n| associated_acts = [[Nickel Creek]], [[Punch Brothers]], [[Mutual Admiration Society (collaboration)|Mutual Admiration Society]], [[Mike Marshall (bluegrass musician)|Mike Marshall]], [[Edgar Meyer]], [[The Goat Rodeo Sessions]], [[Vulfpeck]]\n| website         = {{URL|www.christhile.com}}\n}}\n'''Christopher Scott Thile''' ({{IPAc-en|\u02c8|\u03b8|i\u02d0|l|i}};<ref>{{cite AV media |date=August 5, 2013 |title=Mandolin Master Chris Thile Plays Bluegrass and Bach |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2LUPtADLYjM  |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/youtube/20211221/2LUPtADLYjM |archive-date=2021-12-21 |url-status=live|access-date=March 12, 2018 |location=YouTube |publisher=[[PBS NewsHour]] }}{{cbignore}}</ref> born February 20, 1981) is an American [[mandolin]]ist, singer, songwriter, composer, and radio personality, best known for his work in the progressive acoustic trio [[Nickel Creek]] and the acoustic folk and progressive bluegrass quintet [[Punch Brothers]]. He is a [[MacArthur Fellows Program|2012 MacArthur Fellow]].<ref>{{cite news|title=2012 MacArthur Foundation 'Genius Grant' Winners|url=http://bigstory.ap.org/article/2012-macarthur-foundation-genius-grant-winners#overlay-context=users/rjagodzinski|date=1 October 2012|agency=Associated Press|access-date=October 1, 2012|archive-date=October 2, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121002000603/http://bigstory.ap.org/article/2012-macarthur-foundation-genius-grant-winners#overlay-context=users/rjagodzinski|url-status=dead}}</ref> From 2016 to its cancellation in 2020, he hosted the radio variety show ''[[Live from Here]]''.<ref name=\"aphc\">{{cite news |url=http://www.avclub.com/article/garrison-keillors-reign-terror-over-americas-airwa-221476 |newspaper=[[The A.V. Club]] |date=June 27, 2015 |last=Hughes |first=William |title=Garrison Keillor's Reign of Terror over America's Airwaves Finally Set to End}}</ref><ref name=\"Bream20161015\">{{cite news |last=Bream |first=Jon |url=http://www.startribune.com/chris-thile-seems-right-at-home-as-new-host-of-a-prairie-home-companion/397212461/#1 |title=Chris Thile seems right at home as new 'Prairie Home Companion' host |work=[[Star Tribune]] |date=October 15, 2016 |access-date=2016-10-16 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url= https://www.livefromhere.org/about/history | title= A Brief History about Live from Here | author=  | date= December 18, 2017 | website= Livefromhere.org | access-date= December 18, 2017 | archive-date= December 22, 2017 | archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20171222050757/https://www.livefromhere.org/about/history/ | url-status= dead }}</ref>\n\n==Biography==\nThe three members of Nickel Creek met in 1989 at [[Carlsbad, California]]'s That Pizza Place, listening to weekly bluegrass shows with their parents. Their first album, ''[[Little Cowpoke]]'', was released on December 31, 1993. Later albums included ''[[Nickel Creek (album)|Nickel Creek]]'' and ''[[This Side]]'', which went platinum and won a [[Grammy Awards of 2003#Folk|Grammy]] for Best Contemporary Folk Album, respectively.<ref>{{cite web|title=Past Winners Search {{!}} 2002|url=http://www.grammy.com/nominees/search?artist=&title=&year=2002&genre=All|website=The GRAMMYs|access-date=2 December 2016}}</ref> In 2005, Nickel Creek released ''[[Why Should the Fire Die?]]'', which received critical acclaim and sold 250,000 units.<ref>[http://indiehq.com/2006/09/20/independent-sales-chart-9-20-06/#more-235]{{Dead link|date=September 2018|bot=InternetArchiveBot|fix-attempted=yes}}</ref>\n\nThile has also released solo albums, including [[Not All Who Wander Are Lost (album)|''Not All Who Wander Are Lost'']] (2001) and 2004's [[Deceiver (Chris Thile album)|''Deceiver'']], on which he wrote, composed, sang, and played every part. In 2008, Thile released a collaboration album with bassist [[Edgar Meyer]], and he also plans to release a collaborative album with [[Hilary Hahn]].<ref name=\"edgarmeyer\">{{cite web | url = http://www.carnegiehall.org/article/box_office/events/evt_8401_ma.html?selecteddate=03172007#0 | title = Tensions Mountain Boys at Carnegie Hall | publisher = [[Carnegie Hall]] | date = March 17, 2007 | access-date = 2007-08-30 | url-status = dead | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20070929083157/http://www.carnegiehall.org/article/box_office/events/evt_8401_ma.html?selecteddate=03172007 | archive-date = September 29, 2007 | df = mdy-all }}</ref><ref name=\"hilaryhahn\">{{cite magazine |url=http://www.allaboutjazz.com/php/news.php?id=15490 |title=Nonesuch Records Signs Singer/Composer/Mandolinist Chris Thile and His New Band, Punch Brothers |magazine=All About Jazz |date=October 9, 2007 |access-date=2007-10-10 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071225112354/http://www.allaboutjazz.com/php/news.php?id=15490 |archive-date=December 25, 2007 |df=mdy }}</ref>\n\n===Personal life===\nIn 2003, Thile married fashion designer Jesse Meighan. The couple divorced in 2004, after 18 months of marriage.<ref>{{Cite news|title = Film Review: How to Grow a Band|date = January 10, 2008|url = http://www.filmjournal.com/filmjournal/content_display/esearch/e3icb95fb02525fc2700dd9e5227d53f03e|publisher = Film Journal|access-date = November 15, 2014|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20141129021244/http://www.filmjournal.com/filmjournal/content_display/esearch/e3icb95fb02525fc2700dd9e5227d53f03e|archive-date = November 29, 2014|url-status = dead}}</ref>\n\nThile married actress [[Claire Coffee]] on December 23, 2013.<ref>{{cite web|title = Mandolinist Chris Thile and Actress Claire Coffee Wed|date = December 25, 2013|url = http://www.cybergrass.com/node/3246|publisher = Cybergrass|access-date = December 25, 2013|website = cybergrass.com|archive-date = December 26, 2013|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20131226012313/http://www.cybergrass.com/node/3246|url-status = dead}}</ref> Coffee and Thile have a son named Calvin Eugene Thile, born on May 15, 2015.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://celebritybabies.people.com/2015/05/15/claire-coffee-welcomes-son-calvin-eugene/|title=Claire Coffee Welcomes Son Calvin Eugene|work=People|date=May 15, 2015|access-date=May 20, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150520214341/http://celebritybabies.people.com/2015/05/15/claire-coffee-welcomes-son-calvin-eugene/|archive-date=May 20, 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n[[Baseball Hall of Fame]] member [[Sam Thompson]] is Thile's great-great-great-great-uncle.<ref>{{Twitter|christhile/statuses/488351338091520002|Chris Thile Tweet}}</ref>\n\n==History==\n\n===1981\u20132000: Early life and career===\nThile was born in [[Oceanside, California]], in 1981. His earliest memories of music are listening to [[Stan Getz]]'s recording of \"[[The Girl from Ipanema]]\" before he even turned one year old. When he was two, his family started going to That Pizza Place, where he listened to John Moore's band Bluegrass Etc. When Thile was four, his family moved to [[Idyllwild, California]].\n\nThile began playing the mandolin at the age of five, taking occasional lessons from John Moore. At age eight, Thile's family and the Watkins family formed [[Nickel Creek]]. The band performed at many California bluegrass festivals, and as a result Chris had to be [[homeschooling|home-schooled]]. At age twelve, he won the mandolin championship at the [[Walnut Valley Festival]] in [[Winfield, Kansas]].\n\nThat same year, 1993, Thile made a demo tape and sent it to the Sugar Hill and Rounder record labels. Both labels showed interest, but the Thiles went with Sugar Hill.<ref>{{cite web | url = http://www.ibluegrass.com/bg_posting3.CFM?p__i=426&p__r=&p__a=inter | title = Chris Thile: Covering the Bases | publisher = iBluegrass.com | date = May 20, 1999 | access-date = 2007-08-30 | url-status = dead | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20071121182607/http://www.ibluegrass.com/bg_posting3.CFM?p__i=426&p__r=&p__a=inter | archive-date = November 21, 2007 | df = mdy-all }}</ref> The next year, Chris Thile released his first solo album, ''[[Leading Off]]'', featuring mostly original compositions.\n\nIn 1995, the Thile family moved to [[Murray, Kentucky]], where Chris' father Scott Thile accepted a position at [[Murray State University]] as a musical instrument technician.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.waynerice.com/bgbios/bgbiosn.htm |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141214081710/http://waynerice.com/bgbios/bgbiosn.htm |archive-date=December 14, 2014 |title=N}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://campus.murraystate.edu/staff/scott.thile/index.html|title=Scott E. Thile|publisher=Campus.murraystate.edu|access-date=February 13, 2015|archive-date=October 13, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111013134640/http://campus.murraystate.edu/staff/scott.thile/index.html|url-status=dead}}</ref> In 1997, Chris released ''[[Stealing Second]]'' and Nickel Creek released ''[[Here to There]]''. Chris went on to attend [[Murray State University]] for a few semesters, where he was a music major.<ref name=\"bases\"/> In 2000, he went to [[Nashville]] to play mandolin on [[Dolly Parton]]'s bluegrass/Appalachian folk album ''[[Little Sparrow]]''.\n\n===2001\u20132005: ''Wander'' and ''Deceiver''===\n{{Main|Not All Who Wander Are Lost (album)|Deceiver (Chris Thile album)}}\nFollowing the major success of the album ''[[Nickel Creek (album)|Nickel Creek]]'', Thile released ''[[Not All Who Wander Are Lost (album)|Not All Who Wander Are Lost]]'' in 2001. The album featured guest appearances from several well-known instrumentalists such as Stuart Duncan, [[B\u00e9la Fleck]], [[Edgar Meyer]], [[Jerry Douglas]], and [[Bryan Sutton]].\n\nIn 2003, Thile teamed up with mandolinist [[Mike Marshall (bluegrass musician)|Mike Marshall]] for the duet album ''Into the Cauldron'', which included original pieces as well as pieces by [[Charlie Parker]] and [[J. S. Bach]]. Also in 2003, Thile joined [[Mark O'Connor]] for his double CD set \"Thirty-Year Retrospective\" which was nominated for a Grammy. In 2004, Thile released ''[[Deceiver (Chris Thile album)|Deceiver]]'', an experimental album on which he recorded every track himself. This included electric guitar, piano, drums, violin, viola, cello, and bass. ''Deceiver'' demonstrated some pop/rock songwriting in addition to \"newgrass\".\n\n===2006\u2013present: Punch Brothers and Edgar Meyer project===\n{{Main|How to Grow a Woman from the Ground|Punch (album)}}\n[[File:Chris Thile 2008 3.jpg|thumb|upright=1.2|Chris Thile with Punch Brothers at Wintergrass, 2008]]\nIn August 2006, Nickel Creek announced that at the end of the year, they would no longer be recording together as a group, and their tour scheduled through 2007 would be their last for an indefinite period of time. In February 2014, the group announced that it would be releasing another album.\n\nThile was a judge for the fifth annual Independent Music Awards to support independent artists' careers.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.independentmusicawards.com/ima_new/pastjudges.asp |title=Past Judges for the Independent Music Awards Include |publisher=Independentmusicawards.com |access-date=February 13, 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110713024722/http://www.independentmusicawards.com/ima_new/pastjudges.asp |archive-date=July 13, 2011 |df=mdy }}</ref>\n\nIn 2006, Thile formed [[Punch Brothers|How to Grow a Band]], with whom he recorded ''[[How to Grow a Woman from the Ground]]'', Thile's fifth album. In an interview with the ''Nashville City Paper'', Thile described the band's formation:\n{{blockquote|We got together one night just to drop a ton of money, drink too much wine, eat steaks, and commiserate about our failed relationships. We had gotten to play together a few days before and we had said that we needed to do something musical together. With our hearts smashed to pieces, it became more urgent \u2013 our lives had gone the same way for so long. I knew I wanted to have a band with Gabe [Witcher], but I didn't know if it would be a rock ensemble, an ambitious acoustic classical thing or a bluegrass group. We played, and there was a serious, instantaneous connection. Then I knew I wanted to put together a bluegrass band \u2013 one with a lot of range, but aesthetically a bluegrass band.<ref>{{cite web | url = http://nashvillecitypaper.com/index.cfm?section=12&screen=news&news_id=51705  | title = Nickel Creek's Thile 'grows' a new band | publisher = Nashville City Paper | date = August 23, 2006 | access-date = 2007-10-13 |archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20060826212803/http://nashvillecitypaper.com/index.cfm?section=12&screen=news&news_id=51705 |archive-date = August 26, 2006}}</ref>\n}}\n\nThe band consisted of Chris Thile (mandolin), [[Gabe Witcher]] (fiddle/violin), [[Chris Eldridge]] (guitar), Greg Garrison (bass), and [[Noam Pikelny]] (banjo). [[Bryan Sutton]] has also filled in on guitar when necessary while Eldridge played out commitments to [[The Infamous Stringdusters]]. In 2007, the band officially changed its name first to \"The Tensions Mountain Boys\" and then \"[[Punch Brothers]]\".\n\nOn March 17, 2007, at [[Carnegie Hall]], this group debuted Thile's ambitious \"The Blind Leaving the Blind\", a 40-minute suite in four movements that Thile told [[NPR]] was written in part to deal with his 2004 divorce.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/2008/02/29/69406288/bluegrass-suite-packs-a-progressive-punch|title=Bluegrass Suite Packs a Progressive 'Punch'|date=February 29, 2008|work=NPR.org|access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref>\n\n[[File:Chris Thile 2008 1.jpg|thumb|left|upright=1.2|Chris Thile with Punch Brothers at Wintergrass, 2008]]\nPunch Brothers released its first album, \"[[Punch (album)|Punch]]\", February 26, 2008, on [[Nonesuch Records]]. The album featured Thile's suite \"The Blind Leaving the Blind\", as well as other original songs.<ref name=\"hilaryhahn\" />\n\nTo promote \"Punch\", Thile and Punch Brothers planned a year-long tour in 2008, as well as a February 29 appearance on ''[[The Tonight Show with Jay Leno]]''.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.nbc.com/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno/calendar/02252008.shtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090331114400/http://www.nbc.com/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno/calendar/02252008.shtml |archive-date=March 31, 2009 |title=Show Calendar}}</ref> In late 2008, Paul Kowert replaced Garrison on bass. Punch Brothers released ''[[Antifogmatic (album)|Antifogmatic]]'' on February 15, 2010, and continued to tour. On November 5, 2010, the band performed \"Rye Whiskey\" on the ''[[Late Show with David Letterman]]'' with [[Steve Martin]] guesting on banjo.\n\nPunch Brothers released their third album, [[Who's Feeling Young Now?]], in early 2012.\n\nIn November 2014, Punch Brothers released a single entitled \"I Blew It Off\", from their then-untitled fourth album. In December 2014, the band announced the scheduled release of an upcoming album and simultaneous release of another new single, \"Julep\".\n\nIn August 2008, Thile and [[double bass|bassist]] [[Edgar Meyer]] announced the release date of the duo's planned debut album. The album was released on Thile's label [[Nonesuch Records]] on September 23, 2008.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nonesuch.com/journal/chris-thile-edgar-meyer-preview-new-album-at-aspen|title=Chris Thile, Edgar Meyer Preview New Album at Aspen|work=Nonesuch Records Official Website|date=August 13, 2008 |access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref> Commenting on the collaboration, Thile said \"Edgar is one of the biggest influences on my musical life, and now I'm in a duo with him and writing songs with him. This was my dream. I always wondered what it would be like to be playing music this hard.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nonesuch.com/albums/edgar-meyer-and-chris-thile|title=Edgar Meyer and Chris Thile|work=Nonesuch Records Official Website|date=September 23, 2008 |access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref> The duo toured in September and October 2008 to promote the album.\n\nIn 2012, Thile won a [[MacArthur Fellows Program|MacArthur Fellowship]].<ref>{{cite web|last1=Rao|first1=Mallika|title=Chris Thile, Youngest MacArthur Genius of 2012, On His 'Dauntingly Lofty' New Status|url=https://www.carolinaperformingarts.org/the-overture/interview-chris-thile-youngest-macarthur-genius-of-2012-on-his-dauntingly-lofty-new-status/|website=Carolinaperformingarts.org|access-date=September 1, 2014|archive-date=September 3, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140903103919/https://www.carolinaperformingarts.org/the-overture/interview-chris-thile-youngest-macarthur-genius-of-2012-on-his-dauntingly-lofty-new-status/|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn 2014, Thile recorded a new collaborative album with [[Edgar Meyer]] entitled [[Bass & Mandolin]] and embarked on a tour with Meyer to support the album.<ref>{{cite web|title=Nonesuch Releases Chris Thile and Edgar Meyer's \"Bass & Mandolin\" on September 9|url=http://www.nonesuch.com/journal/nonesuch-releases-chris-thile-edgar-meyer-bass-mandolin-september-9-2014-08-06|website=www.nonesuch.com|date=August 6, 2014 |access-date=September 1, 2014}}</ref>\n\nAlso in 2014, Thile reunited with Nickel Creek to release a new album called ''[[A Dotted Line]]'' in celebration of their 25th anniversary. The group also embarked on a national tour titled NC25.<ref name=\"nonesuch\">[http://www.nonesuch.com/journal/nonesuch-releases-first-nickel-creek-album-nine-years-a-dotted-line-april-1-2014-02-18 \"Nonesuch Releases First Nickel Creek Album in Nine Years, \"A Dotted Line,\" April 1\"]. ''[[Nonesuch Records]]''. February 18, 2014. Retrieved February 18, 2014.</ref>\n\nPunch Brothers released [[The Phosphorescent Blues]], their fourth album, and The Wireless EP in 2015. They also released their fifth and sixth albums, [[All Ashore (album)]] and [[Hell on Church Street]], in 2018 and 2022 respectively.\n\n===Side projects===\n[[File:Amazing David Grisman, Chris Thile, Enrique Coria Winterhawk (Greyfox) Bluegrass Festival 1998.webm|thumb|right|[[David Grisman]], Chris Thile and [[Enrique Coria]] at the [[Grey Fox Bluegrass Festival]]  in 1998]]\nThile is featured in the documentary ''Bluegrass Journey'', along with the rest of Nickel Creek. He has also appeared on a number of other artists' recordings, including [[B\u00e9la Fleck]]'s ''[[Perpetual Motion (album)|Perpetual Motion]]'', playing arrangements of Baroque, Impressionist, Classical and other styles of music with Fleck and Edgar Meyer; ''Jam Session'', with [[Mark O'Connor]], [[Frank Vignola]], [[Bryan Sutton]], and Jon Burr; the [[Dixie Chicks]]' ''Home'', [[Kate Rusby]]'s ''[[Awkward Annie]]'', [[Julie Fowlis]]'s ''[[Cuilidh]]'', [[Dolly Parton]]'s ''[[Little Sparrow]]'', [[Dierks Bentley]]'s ''Up on the Ridge'', [[Jacob Collier]]'s \"[[Djesse Vol. 2]]\", and [[Sarah Jarosz]]'s ''Song Up in Her Head'' and ''Follow Me Down''.\n\nThile has performed as a duo with guitarist and vocalist Michael Daves since 2005.<ref>{{cite web|last=Klein|first=Bradley|title=Chris Thile and Michael Daves Interview|url=http://www.mandolincafe.com/news/publish/mandolins_001351.shtml|publisher=Mandolin Cafe|access-date=May 9, 2011}}</ref> They released their debut album, ''Sleep With One Eye Open'', on May 10, 2011. Recorded at [[Jack White (musician)|Jack White]]'s studio, the album consists of 16 classic bluegrass duets. Jack White also produced and played on the duo's 7\" vinyl record ''Man in the Middle'' on [[Third Man Records]]. Thile and Daves met in 2005 at a bluegrass jam at NYC's Baggot Inn.\n\nIn 2009 Thile completed a mandolin concerto entitled ''Ad astra per alas porci''. The work was commissioned by a consortium of orchestras including the [[Colorado Symphony Orchestra]], [[Los Angeles Chamber Orchestra]], [[Oregon Symphony]], [[Alabama Symphony Orchestra]], [[Winston-Salem Symphony]], [[Delaware Symphony Orchestra]], [[Portland Symphony Orchestra]], and [[Interlochen Center for the Arts]]. Thile performed the world premiere of the first movement with the Interlochen Arts Camp World Youth Symphony Orchestra under director [[Jung-Ho Pak]], and premiered his entire concerto with the [[Colorado Symphony Orchestra]] on September 17, 2009.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nonesuch.com/journal/chris-thile-premieres-his-mandolin-concerto-with-colorado-symphony-2009-09-16|title=Chris Thile Premieres His Mandolin Concerto with Colorado Symphony|work=Nonesuch Records Official Website|date=September 16, 2009 |access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nonesuch.com/journal/oregonian-chris-thile-reinvents-his-instrument-with-mandolin-concerto-2009-09-29|title=Oregonian: Chris Thile Reinvents His Instrument with Mandolin Concerto|work=Nonesuch Records Official Website|date=September 29, 2009 |access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.bluegrassjournal.com/2009/09/01/chris-thile-composes-mandolin-concerto/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120219132849/http://www.bluegrassjournal.com/2009/09/01/chris-thile-composes-mandolin-concerto/ |archive-date=February 19, 2012 |title=Chris Thile composes Mandolin Concerto |first=Dan |last=Tackett |date=September 1, 2009}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.violinist.com/blog/laurie/20099/10496/|title=Reviews of Chris Thile's Mandolin Concerto|publisher=Violinist.com|access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref>\n\nIn 2011, he recorded ''[[The Goat Rodeo Sessions]]'' with cellist [[Yo-Yo Ma]], bassist [[Edgar Meyer]] and fiddle player [[Stuart Duncan]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.yo-yoma.com/music/goat-rodeo-sessions|title=The Goat Rodeo Sessions|work=The Official Yo-Yo Ma Site|access-date=February 13, 2015|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150214034542/http://www.yo-yoma.com/music/goat-rodeo-sessions|archive-date=February 14, 2015|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On October 25, 2011, he appeared on the Tonight Show as a member of the Yo-Yo Ma and Friends musical act.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nbc.com/the-tonight-show/episodes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111022010811/http://www.nbc.com/the-tonight-show/episode-guide/|url-status=dead|title=Watch The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon Episodes at NBC.com|archive-date=October 22, 2011|access-date=July 17, 2021|website=Nbc.com}}</ref> On June 19, 2020, the same group of musicians released a second album entitled ''[[Not Our First Goat Rodeo]]''.\n\nThile released a solo album entitled ''Bach: Sonatas and Partitas, Vol. 1'' in June 2013. The work comprises three works by [[Johann Sebastian Bach]] written for solo violin: Sonata No. 1 in G minor, BWV 1001; Partita No. 1 in B minor, BWV 1002; and Sonata No. 2 in A minor, BWV 1003.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nonesuch.com/journal/nonesuch-releases-chris-thile-bach-sonatas-partitas-vol-1-august-6-2013-06-19 |title=Nonesuch Releases Chris Thile's \"Bach: Sonatas and Partitas, Vol. 1\" on August 6 &#124; Nonesuch Records |date=June 19, 2013 |publisher=Nonesuch.com |access-date=2017-10-18}}</ref>\n\nFor 2018\u201319, Thile was named to the [[Barbara Knowles Debs|Richard and Barbara Debs Composer's Chair]] at [[Carnegie Hall]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nonesuch.com/journal/chris-thile-carnegie-hall-debs-composers-chair-2018-19-season-2018-01-25 |title=Chris Thile to Hold Carnegie Hall Debs Composer's Chair for 2018\u201319 Season &#124; Nonesuch Records |publisher=Nonesuch.com |date=2018-01-25 |access-date=2019-03-15}}</ref>\n\nIn 2021 the artist was inter alia part of the [[Newport Folk Festival]] in July.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Newport Folk Festival stage schedule 2021 |url=https://newportfolk.org/2021-schedule/ |access-date=2021-09-21 |website=newportfolk.org}}</ref>\n\nIn 2024, Thile provided the singing voice and mandolin performance of Wendell in the [[Country Bear Jamboree#Musical Jamboree|Country Bear Musical Jamboree]] at [[Walt Disney World]]'s [[Magic Kingdom]].\n\n===''A Prairie Home Companion / Live from Here''===\n{{main|Live from Here}}\n[[File:2016-01-30CarlileJaroszThilePunchBrosAPHC.jpg|thumb|right|Thile hosting ''A Prairie Home Companion'' with guest [[Brandi Carlile]]]]\nThile made his first appearance on [[Garrison Keillor]]'s radio show ''[[A Prairie Home Companion]]'' in 1996, at age 15 and has returned numerous times\u2014as a solo artist, with Nickel Creek, and with Punch Brothers. On February 7 and 14 in 2015 and January 30 and February 6, 2016, he was the show's guest host. \n<ref>{{cite web\n |url          = http://prairiehome.org/special-guest-host-chris-thile-february-2015/\n |title        = Special Guest Host Chris Thile \u2013 February 7 & 14, 2015\n |author       = <!--Staff writer(s); no by-line.-->\n |date         = February 3, 2015\n |website      = prairiehome.org\n |access-date  = 2015-04-03\n |archive-url  = https://web.archive.org/web/20160304084457/http://prairiehome.org/special-guest-host-chris-thile-february-2015/\n |archive-date = March 4, 2016\n |url-status     = dead\n |df           = mdy-all\n}}</ref> On July 21, 2015, Keillor officially announced that he was leaving the show and that Thile would succeed him as permanent host in 2016.<ref>{{cite web |\nurl= http://www.thebluegrasssituation.com/read/chris-thile-become-full-time-host-prairie-home-companion|\ntitle= It's official: chris thile to become full time host of 'a prairie home companion'|\nauthor=Cameron Matthews |\ndate= July 21, 2015|\nwebsite= thebluegrasssituation.com|\naccess-date= 2015-07-21\n}}</ref>  Thile's first show as host took place on October 15, 2016, at the [[Fitzgerald Theater]] in St. Paul.<ref name=\"Bream20161015\"/> On February 18, 2017, Thile announced that his version of the show had been renewed for another season.  On December 16, 2017, at the Town Hall theater in New York, Thile announced that the show would be renamed ''[[Live from Here]]''. The show continued airing live on public radio until its final show, on May 30, 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Live from Here with Chris Thile Episodes|url=https://www.livefromhere.org/shows|access-date=2020-07-30|website=www.livefromhere.org|language=en|archive-date=June 26, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200626070025/https://www.livefromhere.org/shows|url-status=dead}}</ref> [[American Public Media]], the producer of the show, halted production as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic's effect on shows with live audiences;<ref>{{Cite web|title=About the Show {{!}} Live from Here with Chris Thile|url=https://www.livefromhere.org/pages/about|access-date=2020-07-30|website=www.livefromhere.org|language=en}}</ref> on June 14, 2020, Minnesota Public Radio announced the show's cancellation.<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Hudak |first1=Joseph |title='Live From Here With Chris Thile' Canceled Because of COVID-19 Pandemic |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/live-from-here-chris-thile-canceled-covid-1016113/ |magazine=Rolling Stone |access-date=8 July 2020}}</ref>\n\n==Awards and nominations==\n* 1996 \u2013 Nominated for [[Grammy Award for Best Country Instrumental Performance]] for \"Scotland\" from ''True Life Blues: The Songs of [[Bill Monroe]]''\n* 1997 \u2013 [[International Bluegrass Music Contemporary Folk Album]] for ''[[This Side]]'' (with [[Nickel Creek]])\n* 2005 \u2013 Nominated for [[Grammy Award for Best Engineered Album, Non-Classical]] for ''[[Deceiver (Chris Thile This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Del_McCoury","to":"Del McCoury"}],"pages":{"2253954":{"pageid":2253954,"ns":0,"title":"Del McCoury","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American bluegrass musician}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2023}}\n{{third-party|date=March 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Del McCoury\n| image           = Del-mccoury-fls.jpg\n| image_size      =\n| caption         = McCoury in 2007\n| birth_name      = Delano Floyd McCoury\n| alias           =\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1939|2|1}}\n| birth_place     = [[Bakersville, North Carolina]]<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.bluegrasshall.org/inductees/delano-floyd-del-mccoury/#:~:text=Delano%20Floyd%20%E2%80%9CDel%E2%80%9D%20McCoury%20was,York%20County%20in%20southeastern%20Pennsylvania |title=Hall of Fame Inductees: Del McCoury |website=Bluegrass Music Hall of Fame & Museum |access-date=January 17, 2021}}</ref> or [[York, Pennsylvania]]<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.delmccouryband.com/|title=Del McCoury Band|website=Del McCoury Band}}</ref>\n| death_date      =\n| genre           = {{hlist|[[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]]|[[Country music|country]]|[[Old-time music|old-time]]}}\n| occupation      = Singer, musician\n| instrument      = Vocals, guitar, banjo\n| years_active    = 1958\u2013present\n| label           = [[Rounder Records]], McCoury Music\n| current_member_of = [[Del McCoury Band]]\n| past_member_of = [[The GrooveGrass Boyz]]\n| website         = {{URL|www.delmccouryband.com}}\n}}\n'''Delano Floyd McCoury''' (born February 1, 1939) is an American [[bluegrass music]]ian. As leader of the [[Del McCoury Band]], he plays guitar and sings lead vocals along with his two sons, [[Ronnie McCoury]] and [[Rob McCoury]], who play mandolin and banjo respectively. In June 2010, he received a [[National Heritage Fellowship]] lifetime achievement award from the [[National Endowment for the Arts]] and in 2011 he was elected into the [[International Bluegrass Music Hall of Fame]].\n\n==Career==\nMcCoury has had a long career in bluegrass. Although originally hired as banjo player, he sang lead vocals and played rhythm guitar for [[Bill Monroe]]'s Blue Grass Boys in 1963,<ref>{{cite book |first1=Kurt |last1=Wolff |first2=Orla |last2=Duane |title=Country Music: The Rough Guide |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=3Jorozp1yp4C&pg=PA234 |year=2000 |publisher=[[Rough Guides]] |isbn=978-1-85828-534-4 |pages=234\u2013235}}</ref> with whom he first appeared on the ''[[Grand Ole Opry]]''. McCoury briefly appeared with the [[Golden State Boys]] in 1964 before taking a series of day jobs in construction and logging, while continuing to work as an amateur musician in Maryland, Virginia and Pennsylvania.<ref name=\"GACTV\">{{cite web |url=http://www.gactv.com/musicbeat/dmccoury120505.html |title=Del McCoury makes bluegrass a family affair |website=[[Great American Family|GACTV]] |date=December 5, 2005 |access-date=February 11, 2006 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060110154435/http://www.gactv.com/musicbeat/dmccoury120505.html |archive-date=January 10, 2006}}</ref>\n\nIn the 1980s his sons began performing with him. Fiddler [[Tad Marks]] and bass player Mike Brantley joined McCoury's group in early 1990s. McCoury's group toured widely throughout the US.<ref>{{cite book |editor-last=Kingsbury |editor-first=Paul |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=untabCgOVkgC&dq=del+McCoury&pg=PA335 |title=The Encyclopedia of Country Music |publisher=[[Oxford University Press]] |year=1998 |page=335 |isbn=9780199770557}}</ref> They relocated to [[Nashville, Tennessee]] as they began to attract attention. Fiddler Jason Carter and bassist Mike Bub joined in 1992. Alan Bartram joined the band as bassist in 2005. McCoury became a member of the Grand Ole Opry in October 2003.\n\nMcCoury was also one of many performers at [[The Clearwater Concert]] at Madison Square Garden on May 3, 2009. The event celebrated the 90th birthday of [[Pete Seeger]].\n\nMcCoury has influenced a great number of bands, including [[Phish]], with whom he has shared the stage several times,<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://phish.net/setlists/2000.html |title=Setlists: 2000 |website=Phish.net}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |url=https://phish.net/setlists/1999.html |title=Setlists: 1999 |website=Phish.net}}</ref> and who have covered his songs.<ref name=\"coversproject.com\">{{cite web |title=Del McCoury Band |url=https://www.coversproject.com/artist/del%20mccoury%20band |website=The Covers Project |access-date=May 27, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180220151920/https://www.coversproject.com/artist/del%20mccoury%20band |archive-date=February 20, 2018}}</ref> He has also performed with [[The String Cheese Incident]] and [[Donna the Buffalo]], and recorded with [[Steve Earle]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Schulman |first1=David |title=Del McCoury: Old-School Music, New Audience |url=https://www.npr.org/2005/06/20/4684144/del-mccoury-old-school-music-new-audience |access-date=May 27, 2023 |work=Morning Edition |publisher=NPR |date=June 20, 2005}}</ref> McCoury has covered songs by artists as diverse as [[The Lovin' Spoonful]], [[Tom Petty]], and [[Richard Thompson (musician)|Richard Thompson]].<ref name=\"coversproject.com\" /> McCoury has appeared at festivals including [[Bonnaroo]], [[High Sierra Music Festival|High Sierra]],<ref name=\"GACTV\" /> the [[Hardly Strictly Bluegrass]], The Telluride Bluegrass Festival, and the [[Newport Folk Festival]].<ref name=\"delmccouryband.com\">{{cite web |title=Del McCoury Band News |url=http://www.delmccouryband.com/news.cfm |website=Del McCoury Band |access-date=May 27, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060721155218/http://www.delmccouryband.com/news.cfm |archive-date=July 21, 2006}}</ref> His television appearances include ''[[Late Night with Conan O'Brien]]'' and the ''[[Late Show with David Letterman]]''.<ref name=\"delmccouryband.com\" /> Del has a very enthusiastic fan base, known as the [[Del-Heads]].\n\n[[Image:Del McCoury Band OSMF 2013 - Ron Baker.jpg|right|thumb|Del McCoury Band \u2013 Old Settler's Music Festival (2013)]]\n\nIn October 2009, The Del McCoury Band began offering fans recordings of their performances on [[USB flash drives]] available immediately after their concerts.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://aderra.net/store/index.php?main_page=product_info&cPath=4&products_id=11 |title=The del McCoury Band Live in Chico CA &#91;20091128DELMC&#93; - $25.00 : Live Concert Recordings on Flash Drives, Aderra USB live music Recordings |website=aderra.net |access-date=January 13, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091227023832/http://aderra.net/store/index.php?main_page=product_info&cPath=4&products_id=11 |archive-date=December 27, 2009 |url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn June 2010, McCoury received a lifetime achievement award from the [[National Endowment for the Arts]] in the field of folk and traditional arts, including a stipend of $25,000.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://archive.nytimes.com/artsbeat.blogs.nytimes.com/2010/06/24/nea-will-honor-18-artists/ |title=NEA Will Honor 18 Artists |first=Kate |last=Taylor |department=ArtsBeat |work=[[The New York Times]] |date=June 24, 2010}}</ref>\n\nIn 2012, he joined the 11th<ref>{{cite web |url=https://independentmusicawards.com/judges/11th-annual-ima-judges/ |title=11th Annual IMA Judges |website=Independent Music Awards |access-date=September 4, 2013}}</ref> annual Independent Music Awards judging panel to assist independent musicians' careers.\n\n==DelFest==\n[[Image:Del McCoury Band Delfest 2009.jpg|thumb|right|Del McCoury Band at 2nd Annual [[DelFest]] (2009)]]\nIn 2008, Del McCoury started [[DelFest]], an annual bluegrass festival in [[Cumberland, Maryland|Cumberland]], Maryland, held at the [[Allegany County Fairgrounds]].<ref name=\"DelFest\">{{Cite web|url=http://delfest.com/|title=Home|website=DelFest.com}}</ref> Del McCoury Band plays every night at each of the festivals.\n\nThe 5th annual DelFest occurred in May 2012,<ref name=\"DelFest\" /> and major bluegrass acts played such as [[Steve Martin]] with the [[Steep Canyon Rangers]], [[Yonder Mountain String Band]], [[Leftover Salmon]], [[Infamous Stringdusters]], [[Railroad Earth]], [[B\u00e9la Fleck]], and [[Sam Bush]], most of which had returned from previous years at the festival.\n\nIn previous years, acts such [[Peter Rowan]], [[David Grisman]], [[Jesse McReynolds]], [[The Avett Brothers]], [[Old Crow Medicine Show]], [[Trampled by Turtles]], [[Greensky Bluegrass]], and [[Psychograss]] have played.\n\nThe 14th DelFest occurred in May 2022, after a two-year delay caused by the [[COVID-19 pandemic in the United States|COVID-19 pandemic]].<ref name=\"DelFest\" />\n\n==Discography==\n\n[[Image:HSB 2005 - Del McCoury.jpg|right|thumb|Del McCoury \u2013 Hardly Strictly Bluegrass (2005)]]\n\n===Solo albums===\n* 1968: ''Del McCoury Sings Bluegrass'' ([[Arhoolie Back to Old Kentucky: A Bill Monroe Celebration'' (Rural Rhythm)\n\n==Awards and honors==\nDel McCoury has won 31 [[International Bluegrass Music Association]] Awards, including Entertainer of the Year four consecutive times<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.pollstar.com/news/viewhotstar.pl?Artist=DELMCR |title=Pollstar -- HotStar the del McCoury Band |access-date=February 11, 2006 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060209045124/http://pollstar.com/news/viewhotstar.pl?Artist=DELMCR |archive-date=February 9, 2006}}</ref> (nine total<ref name=\"delmccouryband.com\" />). McCoury has also won IBMA Male Vocalist of the Year four times. In 2004 he was nominated for the Best Bluegrass Album [[Grammy Award]] for ''It's Just The Night'', and in 2006 he won his first Grammy Award, in the same category, for ''The Company We Keep''.<ref name=\"delmccouryband.com\" /> In 2014, McCoury was nominated and won his second Grammy Award for ''The Streets of Baltimore''.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/artists/del-mccoury |title=Artist: Del McCoury |website=www.grammy.com |publisher=Recording Academy |access-date=January 17, 2021}}</ref> He was a recipient of a 2010 [[National Heritage Fellowship]] awarded by the [[National Endowment for the Arts]], which is the United States government's highest honor in the folk and traditional arts.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.arts.gov/honors/heritage/list?title=&field_year_value=2010 |title=NEA National Heritage Fellowships 2010 |website=www.arts.gov |publisher=National Endowment for the Arts |access-date=January 17, 2021}}</ref> McCoury received the Bluegrass Star Award, presented by the Bluegrass Heritage Foundation, in 2015. The award is bestowed upon bluegrass artists who do an exemplary job of advancing traditional bluegrass music and bringing it to new audiences while preserving its character and heritage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://bluegrassheritage.org/bluegrass-star-award/|title=Bluegrass Heritage Foundation official website|website=Bluegrassheritage.org|year=2010|access-date=December 28, 2015}}</ref>\n\n===International Bluegrass Music Association Awards===\n[[Image:Mccoury-band.jpg|right|thumb|Del McCoury Band, 2007]]\n\n*1990 Male Vocalist of the Year \u2013 Del McCoury<ref This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Norman_Blake_(American_musician)","to":"Norman Blake (American musician)"}],"pages":{"1268563":{"pageid":1268563,"ns":0,"title":"Norman Blake (American musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American musician}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2015}}\n{{BLP sources|date=July 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name             = Norman Blake\n| image            = \n| image_size       = \n| landscape        = yes\n| background       = solo_singer\n| birth_name       = Norman L. Blake\n| birth_date       = {{birth-date and age|March 10, 1938}}\n| birth_place      = [[Chattanooga]], Tennessee, U.S.\n| instrument       = Guitar, mandolin, six-string banjo, fiddle, dobro, banjo, viola, harmonica\n| genre            = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]], [[folk music|folk]], [[Country music|country]]\n| occupation       = Musician, singer-songwriter\n| years_active     = 1954\u2013present\n| label            = [[Rounder Records|Rounder]], [[Flying Fish Records|Flying Fish]], [[Takoma Records|Takoma]], [[Shanachie Records|Shanachie]], [[Red House Records|Red House]], Plectrafone/Western Jubilee\n| spouse           = [[Nancy Blake]]\n| associated_acts  = [[Johnny Cash]], [[Kris Kristofferson]]\n}}\n\n'''Norman L. Blake''' (born March 10, 1938) is a traditional American stringed instrument artist and songwriter. He is half of the eponymous '''Norman & Nancy Blake''' band with his wife, Nancy Blake.\n\n==Music career==\n\n===Early performing===\nBlake was born in [[Chattanooga]], Tennessee, and grew up in [[Sulphur Springs, Alabama]]. He listened to old-time and country music on the radio by [[the Carter Family]], the [[Skillet Lickers]], [[Roy Acuff]], and the Monroe Brothers ([[Charlie Monroe|Charlie]] and [[Bill Monroe]]).<ref name=\"ND\">{{cite web|title=Norman & Nancy Blake - The old-fashioned way|url=https://www.nodepression.com/norman-nancy-blake-the-old-fashioned-way/|website=No Depression|access-date=20 May 2019|date=1 January 2006}}</ref> He learned guitar at age 11 or 12, then [[mandolin]], [[dobro]], and [[fiddle]] in his teens. When he was 16, he dropped out of school to play music professionally.<ref name=\"Stone\">{{cite web|last1=Stone|first1=Steven|title=Norman Blake|url=https://www.vintageguitar.com/2902/norman-blake/|website=Vintage Guitar|access-date=26 November 2016|date=12 December 2003}}</ref>\n\nIn the 1950s, Blake joined the Dixieland Drifters and performed on radio broadcasts, then joined the Lonesome Travelers. When he was drafted in 1961, he served as an Army radio operator in the [[Panama Canal Zone]]. He started a popular band known as the [[Fort Kobbe|Kobbe]] Mountaineers.<ref name=\"Stambler\">{{cite book|last1=Stambler|first1=Irwin|last2=Stambler|first2=Lyndon|title=Folk and blues : the encyclopedia|date=2001|publisher=St. Martin's Press|location=New York|isbn=0312200579|pages=34\u201335|edition=1}}</ref> A year later, while he was on leave, he recorded the album ''Twelve Shades of Bluegrass'' with the Lonesome Travelers.<ref name=\"Wolff\">{{cite web|last1=Wolff|first1=Kurt|title=Norman Blake {{!}} Biography & History {{!}} AllMusic|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/norman-blake-mn0000387352/biography|website=AllMusic|access-date=26 November 2016}}</ref>\n\n===Nashville and Johnny Cash===\nAfter being discharged from the Army, Blake moved to Nashville and became a [[studio musician]].<ref name=\"Stambler\" /> For ten years, he toured and recorded with country singer [[Johnny Cash]]<ref name=\"Wolff\" /> and continued to play with Cash  intermittently over the next thirty.<ref name=\"Stone\" /> He met Nancy Short, a cellist with a [[classical music]] background who was playing in a folk group. He was asked by [[Bob Dylan]] to play on the country-folk album ''[[Nashville Skyline]]'', then became a member of the house band on Johnny Cash's TV show.<ref name=\"ND\" /><ref name=\"Stambler\" /> [[Kris Kristofferson]], one of the guests, hired Blake to tour with him. Blake recorded with folk singer [[Joan Baez]] and appeared on her hit song \"[[The Night They Drove Old Dixie Down]]\".<ref name=\"Wolff\" /> In 1971, he became a member of the bluegrass group Aero-plain, led by multi-instrumentalist [[John Hartford]] with fiddler [[Vassar Clements]], a short-lived project.<ref name=\"Stambler\" /><ref name=\"Wolff\" />\n\nBlake also played dobro on the 1972 album ''[[Will the Circle be Unbroken (Nitty Gritty Dirt Band album)|Will the Circle Be Unbroken]]'' by the [[Nitty Gritty Dirt Band]].<ref name=\"circle\">{{Cite web |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/will-the-circle-be-unbroken-mw0000193505/credits |title=Will the Circle Be Unbroken: Credits |website=AllMusic |access-date=March 19, 2017}}</ref>\n\nIn 1972, Blake recorded his first solo album, ''[[Home in Sulphur Springs]]'' ([[Rounder Records|Rounder]], 1972).<ref name=\"Wolff\" /> Soon after his debut, he and Nancy recorded their first album, ''[[The Fields of November]]'' ([[Flying Fish Records|Flying Fish]], 1974), with Nancy on hillbilly cello. They married in 1975 and performed together for twenty years.<ref name=\"ND\" /><ref name=\"Stambler\" />\n\n===Style===\nMost of the music that Norman Blake plays could be described as neo-traditionalist Americana folk and roots music (folk, bluegrass, country, blues), and many of the songs he plays are [[Traditional music|traditional]], but he plays this acoustic type of music with a style, speed, and quality that has evolved and progressed in the modern age. Though probably best known for his fluid renditions of classic fiddle tunes transcribed for the guitar (\"Fiddler's Dram/Whiskey Before Breakfast\"), Blake has also written songs that have become bluegrass and folk standards, such as \"Ginseng Sullivan\", \"Slow Train through Georgia\", \"Billy Gray\", and \"Church Street Blues\".\n\nBlake has also written and published songs of a political nature, such as \"Don\u2019t Be Afraid of the Neo-Cons.\"<ref name=\":0\" />\n\nBlake is known for his tastefully simple-sounding style, saying, \"I\u2019m more interested in the music and the tone than I am the licks.\"<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite web |last=Campbell |first=Phil |date=2007-11-21 |title=Interview: Norman Blake |url=https://www.fretboardjournal.com/features/interview-norman-blake/ |access-date=2022-11-28 |website=Fretboard Journal |language=en}}</ref>\n\nAlthough known as one of the most prominent steel-string guitar [[flatpicking|flatpickers]], Blake is a multi-instrumentalist and vocalist. Other instruments he plays include the [[mandolin]], [[Guitjo (six-string)|6-string banjo]], [[fiddle]], [[dobro]], [[banjo]] and [[viola]].<ref>CD liner notes from ''The Fields of November'', Flying Fish Records, 1992</ref> He is known for his loose, right-hand guitar technique, which arose out of his mandolin technique. Also well known is his devotion to 12-fret guitars, including Martin 00s, 000s, D18s, D28s, and Gibsons, like his 1929 12-fret Nick Lucas special.\n\n=== Collaborations ===\nBlake has collaborated with [[Tony Rice]] on the albums, \"Blake and Rice,\" and \"Blake and Rice 2,\" which include many tunes, including some of Blake's originals.<ref>{{Citation |last=Tony Rice |title=Blake & Rice |date=1992 |url=https://www.amazon.com/Blake-Rice-Tony-Norman/dp/B0000002HV |publisher=Rounder |language=English |access-date=2022-12-06 |last2=Norman Blake |last3=Norman Blake & Tony Rice}}</ref><ref>{{Citation |last=Tony Rice |title=Blake & Rice 2 |date=1992 |url=https://www.amazon.com/Blake-Rice-2-Norman-Tony/dp/B0000002JB |publisher=Rounder |language=English |access-date=2022-12-06 |last2=Norman Blake |last3=Norman Blake & Tony Rice}}</ref> Blake also released an album with Mike Compton called, \"Gallop to Georgia,\" which showcases many Old-Time tunes.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Mike Compton |url=https://www.mikecompton.net/ |access-date=2022-12-06 |website=Mike Compton |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n===Awards and honors===\nBlake played on the album ''[[Raising Sand]]'' by [[Robert Plant]] and [[Alison Krauss]], which won five Grammy Awards, and on the soundtrack ''[[O Brother, Where Art Thou? (soundtrack)|O Brother, Where Art Thou?]]'', which won a Grammy for [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year|Album of the Year]].\n\nNorman & Nancy Blake received Grammy nominations in the Best Traditional Folk Recording category for ''Blind Dog'', ''Just Gimme Somethin' I'm Used To'', ''While Passing Along This Way'', and ''The Hobo's Last Ride''. In 1986 Norman Blake was chosen Best Multi-Instrumentalist by the readers of ''Frets'' magazine.<ref>[http://www.flatpick.com/Pages/Featured_Artist/norman.html] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130921055726/http://www.flatpick.com/Pages/Featured_Artist/norman.html|date=September 21, 2013}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n* ''[[Home in Sulphur Springs]]'' ([[Rounder Records|Rounder]], 1972)\n* ''[[The Fields of November]]'' ([[Flying Fish Records|Flying Fish]], 1974)\n* ''[[Old and New (album)|Old and New]]'' (Flying Fish, 1975)\n* Made available for public use by the State Archives of Florida.\n{{International Bluegrass Music Hall of Fame}}\n{{Grammy Award for Album of the Year 2000s}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Blake, Norman}}\n[[Category:1938 births]]\n[[Category:American bluegrass guitarists]]\n[[Category:American male guitarists]]\n[[Category:American country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:American folk musicians]]\n[[Category:Bluegrass musicians from Tennessee]]\n[[Category:Grammy Award winners]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:Musicians from Chattanooga, Tennessee]]\n[[Category:American bluegrass mandolinists]]\n[[Category:Singer-songwriters from Tennessee]]\n[[Category:American country fiddlers]]\n[[Category:American country guitarists]]\n[[Category:American session musicians]]\n[[Category:American country banjoists]]\n[[Category:American bluegrass fiddlers]]\n[[Category:Resonator guitarists]]\n[[Category:American violists]]\n[[Category:American country mandolinists]]\n[[Category:Guitarists from Tennessee]]\n[[Category:20th-century American guitarists]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Tennessee]]\n[[Category:20th-century American male musicians]]\n[[Category:Red House Records artists]]\n[[Category:Shanachie Records artists]]\n[[Category:Rounder Records artists]]\n[[Category:Flying Fish Records artists]]\n[[Category:American male singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:20th-century violists]]\n[[Category:American ragtime mandolinists]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_GrooveGrass_Boyz","to":"The GrooveGrass Boyz"}],"pages":{"18972899":{"pageid":18972899,"ns":0,"title":"The GrooveGrass Boyz","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American band}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = The GrooveGrass Boyz\n| image                 = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Nashville]], [[Tennessee]], United States\n| genre               = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]], [[dance music|dance]], [[country music|country]]\n| years_active        = 1996\u20131998\n| label               = [[Imprint Records]]<br>[[Reprise Records|Reprise]]/[[Warner Bros. Records]]\n| past_members        = [[Bootsy Collins]]<br />[[Jerry Douglas]]<br />[[Del McCoury]]<br />Scott Rouse<br />[[Mac Wiseman]]\n}}\n'''The GrooveGrass Boyz''' were an American musical group that played a mix of [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]], [[funk]], and [[freestyle music]]. The group was founded as a side project by record producer and session musician Scott Rouse in 1987, after he began experimenting with dance mixes of bluegrass and country songs, eventually applying the term groovegrass to his mix of music. He then moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee]], and joined several other country musicians and funk bass guitarist [[Bootsy Collins]], releasing a country version of [[Los del R\u00edo]]'s \"[[Macarena]]\" and two albums. The country cover of \"Macarena\" charted on both the [[Hot Country Songs]] charts and the [[Bubbling Under Hot 100]], and was the group's only chart entry.\n\n==History==\nRouse, a [[session musician]] from [[Boston, Massachusetts]], first came up with the idea of GrooveGrass in the mid-1980s when he began experimenting with dance mixes of bluegrass songs such as [[Alton Delmore]]'s \"Deep River Blues\". His mixes became popular at local clubs, eventually leading to one disc jockey terming the blend of music \"groovegrass\".<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web |url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p350665/biography|pure_url=yes}} |title=GrooveGrass biography |accessdate=2008-08-21 |last=Ankeny |first=Jason |publisher=[[Allmusic]]}}</ref>\n\nRouse then moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee]], at the request of his friend, musician [[Doc Watson]]. Rouse's first country remix was for [[Warner Bros. Records|Warner Bros.]] It was a remix of [[John Anderson (musician)|John Anderson]]'s 1983 Number One single \"[[Swingin' (John Anderson song)|Swingin']].\" At Anderson's request, Warner never released the cut, although it became a popular [[bootleg recording]].<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> It was followed by an [[Extended play|EP]] remix of \"[[Rocky Top]]\", which was released and went on to sell more than 100,000 copies in the United States.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> Rouse also produced comedian [[Jeff Foxworthy]]'s trademark \"You might be a redneck if\u2026\" single he named called the \"Redneck Stomp\",<ref name=\"bb\"/> one of several similar musical tracks included on Foxworthy's ''[[Crank It Up: The Music Album]]''.\n\nSoon afterward, Rouse recruited several other musicians, including members of [[Del McCoury]]'s band, funk bass guitarist [[Bootsy Collins]], and bluegrass multi-instrumentalist [[Jerry Douglas]], to perform as the GrooveGrass Boyz.<ref name=\"news\">{{cite web |url=http://www.musiciansnews.com/mastering/18/nashville_producer_scott_rouse_mixing_groovegrass_with_the_u.shtml |title=Nashville producer Scott Rouse Mixing GrooveGrass with the UAD-1 |accessdate=2008-08-21 |work=Musicians' News}}</ref> They saw their most successful release in late 1996, when they put out a country version of the \"[[Macarena (song)|Macarena]]\", a song made popular earlier that year by Spanish duo [[Los del R\u00edo]].<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> The GrooveGrass Boyz' version, released on [[Imprint Records]],<ref name=\"bb\">{{cite magazine |url=http://www.allbusiness.com/retail-trade/miscellaneous-retail-retail-stores-not/4626736-1.html |title=Groovegrass' Scott Rouse Weds Unlikely Pair Of Bluegrass, R&B |accessdate=2008-08-21 |last=Bessman |first=Jim |date=1999-01-09 |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]}}</ref> peaked at No.&nbsp;70 on the [[Hot Country Songs]] charts and No.&nbsp;7 on the [[Bubbling Under Hot 100]]. The single sold over 100,000 copies.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.steamiron.com/twangin/int-groovegrass.html |title=The Mothership Lands at MerleFest: Interview with Groovegrass Mastermind Scott Rouse|accessdate=2009-05-31 |last=Wall |first=Jeff |year=1998|work=Twangin'!}}</ref>  It was followed in 1997 by a self-released album, and in 1998 by another album on [[Reprise Records]]. These included [[Doc Watson]], [[Mac Wiseman]], [[Bernie Leadon]], and other notable artists. Neither album produced any chart single.\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! style=\"width:26em;\"| Title\n! style=\"width:18em;\"| Album details\n|- \n! scope=\"row\"| ''The GrooveGrass Boyz''\n| \n* Release date: 1997\n* Label: self-released\n|- \n! scope=\"row\"| ''GrooveGrass\u00ae 101 featuring the GrooveGrass Boyz\u2122''\n| \n* Release date: November 24, 1998\n* Label: [[Reprise Records|Reprise]]/[[Warner Bros. Records]]\n|}\n\n===Singles===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Year\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:16em;\"| Single\n! colspan=\"2\"| Peak chart<br />positions\n|- style=\"font-size:smaller;\"\n! width=\"45\"| [[Hot Country Songs|US Country]]\n! width=\"45\"| [[Bubbling Under Hot 100|US Bubbling]]\n|-\n| 1996\n! scope=\"row\"| \"Macarena (Country Version)\"\n| 70\n| 7\n|}\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:GrooveGrass Boyz}}\n[[Category:American country music groups]]\n[[Category:American bluegrass music groups]]\n[[Category:Reprise Records artists]]\n[[Category:Musical groups established in 1987]]\n[[Category:Imprint Records artists]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Stanley_Brothers","to":"The Stanley Brothers"}],"pages":{"333239":{"pageid":333239,"ns":0,"title":"The Stanley Brothers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American bluegrass duo}}\n<!--  Commented out because image was deleted: [[Image:Stanley Brothers.jpg|thumb|right|Carter and Ralph Stanley]] -->\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name                = The Stanley Brothers \n| image              = IHearMySaviorCalling.jpg\n| caption            = Label of the Stanley Brothers' single \"I Hear My Savior Calling\"\n| image_size         = \n| background         = group_or_band \n| origin             = [[Dickenson County, Virginia]], U.S.\n| genre              = {{hlist | [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]] | [[Appalachian folk music|Appalachian folk]] | [[country music|country]] | [[gospel music|gospel]]}}\n| years_active       = 1946\u20131966\n| label              = {{hlist | Rich-R-Tone | [[Columbia Records|Columbia]] | [[Mercury Records|Mercury]] | [[King Records (USA)|King]] | [[Starday Records|Starday]] | Wango | Rimrock | [[Old Homestead Records|Old Homestead]]}}\n| past_members       = \n* [[Carter Stanley]]\n* [[Ralph Stanley]]\n}}\n\n'''The Stanley Brothers''' were an American [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]] duo of singer-songwriters and musicians, made up of brothers [[Carter Stanley]] (August 27, 1925 \u2013 December 1, 1966) and [[Ralph Stanley]] (February 25, 1927 \u2013 June 23, 2016).<ref name=\"LarkinGE\">{{cite book|title=The Guinness Encyclopedia of Popular Music|editor=Colin Larkin|publisher=Guinness Publishing|date=1992|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-939-0|pages=2361/2}}</ref> Ralph and Carter performed as The Stanley Brothers with their band, The Clinch Mountain Boys, from 1946 to 1966. Ralph kept the band name when he continued as a solo artist after Carter's death, from 1967 until his own death in 2016.\n\n==Early lives==\nCarter and Ralph Stanley were born on a small farm in [[Dickenson County, Virginia]]. Music was a part of their lives even in their early years, and they listened to the [[Bill Monroe|Monroe Brothers]], [[J. E. Mainer|J.&nbsp;E. Mainer's Mountaineers]] and the [[Grand Ole Opry]] on local radio.\n\n==Careers==\nThe brothers formed a band, the Lazy Ramblers, and performed as a duo on [[WJCW|WJHL]] radio in Johnson City, Tennessee.<ref name=\"country_music\">{{cite book |title= Country Music: The Encyclopedia| edition= 3rd |last= Stambler|first= Irwin|author2=Grelun Landon |year= 2000|publisher= St. Martin's Press|location= New York|isbn= 0-312-26487-9|pages= 457\u20138|url= https://books.google.com/books?id=d18K8QWcEo8C|access-date= February 6, 2010}}</ref> World War II interrupted their musical career, but once both brothers returned from the United States Army, they resumed their musical pursuits. They formed their band, the Stanley Brothers and the [[Clinch Mountain Boys]], in the month of November 1946<ref>Back of 33rpm album cover \"In Memory of Carter Stanley/ An Empty Mansion by The Stanley Brothers. Testimonial story by Ralph Stanley. Old Homestead Records OHCS 118.</ref> as the first band to copy the [[Bill Monroe|Monroe sound]].<ref name=mmc426>Malone, McCulloh 1975, p.&nbsp;426.</ref> Carter played guitar and sang lead, while Ralph played [[banjo]] and sang with a strong, high [[tenor]] voice. Additional members of this early band were [[Pee Wee Lambert|Darrell \"Pee Wee\" Lambert]] on [[mandolin]] and Bobby Sumner on [[fiddle]]. Sumner soon was replaced by [[Leslie Keith]].<ref name=r80>Rosenberg 2005, p.&nbsp;80.</ref>\n\nOn December 26, 1946, the band began performing at radio station [[WZAP|WCYB]] in Bristol, Tennessee as stalwarts of the famed ''Farm and Fun Time'' radio show.<ref name=w3>Wright 1995, p.&nbsp;3.</ref> They made their recording debut in September 1947 for [[Rich-R-Tone Records]] which had been founded the year before. Their records sold well, \"outselling even [[Eddy Arnold]]\" regionally.<ref name=r82>Rosenberg 2005, p.&nbsp;82.</ref> Up to now, Ralph had been playing his banjo with two fingers on recordings and in concerts, but in 1948, he switched to the three-finger style (popularised by [[Earl Scruggs]]).<ref name=r84>Rosenberg 2005, p.&nbsp;84.</ref> In March 1949, the Stanley Brothers began recording for [[Columbia Records]].<ref name=r87>Rosenberg 2005, p.&nbsp;87.</ref> During this time, [[Bill Monroe]] was not particularly fond of groups like the Stanley Brothers and [[Flatt & Scruggs]] who he believed \"stole\" his music by copying it; they were seen as \"economic threats.\"<ref name=s88>Rosenberg 2005, p.&nbsp;88.</ref><ref name=r85>Rosenberg 2005, p.&nbsp;85.</ref>\n\nFinancially hard times in the early 1950s forced the brothers to take a short break in their musical career. They began working for the [[Ford Motor Company]] in Detroit. Eventually, Monroe and the Stanley Brothers became friends, and Carter performed for several months with Bill Monroe in the summer of 1951. In August 1951, Ralph was involved in a serious automobile accident that almost ended his career.<ref name=w4>Wright 1995, p.&nbsp;4.</ref> Following his recovery, Carter and Ralph reunited to front their Clinch Mountain Boys.\n\nAs bluegrass music grew less popular in the late 1950s, the Stanley Brothers moved to Live Oak, Florida and headlined the weekly ''Suwannee River Jamboree'' radio show on [[WQHL (AM)|WNER]] from 1958 to 1962. The three-hour show was also syndicated across the Southeast.<ref>{{cite web\n| title = Folklife Database: Recording of the Suwannee River Jamboree radio program\n| work = floridamemory.com\n| publisher = State Library and Archives of Florida\n| url = http://www.floridamemory.com/Collections/folklife/profile.cfm?idsThing=4476\n| access-date = 2009-05-20}}\n\n</ref> In 1966, the brothers toured Europe, and upon returning home, they continued to perform together until Carter's death in December 1966.<ref name=w5>Wright 1995, p.&nbsp;5.</ref>\n\nMany years later, Ralph revived the Clinch Mountain Boys until his death in 2016. He performed with them through 2013. He recorded one last album in 2014, ''Side By Side'', with his son, Ralph II. Among the musicians who have played in the revived Clinch Mountain Boys were [[Ricky Skaggs]], [[Keith Whitley]], [[Larry Sparks]], [[Curly Ray Cline]], Jack Cooke, Roy Lee Centers, Charlie Sizemore, Ray Goins, and Ralph Stanley II. Ralph's career received a big boost with his prominent role on the very successful soundtrack recording of the 2000 feature film, ''[[O Brother, Where Art Thou?]]'', which featured the song \"[[Man of Constant Sorrow]]\" among others.\n\n==Legacy==\nThe Stanley Brothers were inducted into the [[International Bluegrass Music Hall of Honor]] in 1992. In 2005, The Barter State Theatre of Virginia premiered an original stage production, ''Man of Constant Sorrow: The Story of the Stanley Brothers'', written by Dr. Douglas Pote.\n\nThe University Press of Mississippi published the first full-length biography of the Stanley Brothers, ''Lonesome Melodies: The Lives and Music of the Stanley Brothers'' by David W. Johnson, on February 1, 2013. The paperback edition was published March 1, 2014.\n\n==Selected recordings==\nAmong the Stanley Brothers' best known recordings are:\n\n*''I'm a Man of Constant Sorrow'' (Columbia 20816, Rec: Nov. 3, 1950, Released: May, 1951)\n*''Rank Stranger''\n*''Angel Band'' (1955)\n*''How Mountain Girls Can Love''\n*''How Far to Little Rock?'' (novelty)\n*''Still Trying to Get to Little Rock (novelty)''\n*''Ridin' That Midnite Train''\n*''Clinch Mountain Backstep''\n*''She's More to Be Pitied''\n*''The Memory of Your Smile''\n*''Love Me Darlin' Just Tonight''\n\n==Clinch Mountain Boys members==\n*[[Carter Stanley]] (lead vocalist, steel-string guitar)\n*[[Ralph Stanley]] (banjo)\n*[[George Shuffler]] (steel-string guitar, bass)\n*Darrell \"Pee Wee\" Lambert (mandolin)\n*Jim Williams (mandolin)\n*Curly Lambert (mandolin, steel-string guitar)\n*[[James Price (fiddle player)|James Price]] (fiddle)\n*Robert \"Bobby\" Sumner (fiddle)\n*Lester Woodie (fiddle) (died 2018)<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://bluegrasstoday.com/les-woodie-passes/|title=Les Woodie passes|website=Blugrasstoday.com|date=March 26, 2018}}</ref>\n*Ralph Mayo (fiddle, steel-string guitar)\n*Chubby Anthony (fiddle)\n*Art Stamper (fiddle)\n*Joe Meadows (fiddle)\n*Paul Moon Mullins (fiddle)\n*Red Stanley (fiddle)\n*Don Miller (fiddle)\n*Vernon Derrick (fiddle, steel-string guitar)\n*[[Curly Ray Cline]] (fiddle) \n*James \"Jay\" Hughes (bass)\n*Ernie Newton (bass)\n*[[James \"Chick\" Stripling]] (bass)\n*[[Mike Seeger]] (bass)\n*[[Charlie Cline]] (steel-string guitar)\n*Bill Napier (steel-string guitar mandolin)\n*Albert Elliott (mandolin, bass, and baritone vocals) better known as [[Touser Murphy]] as his stage name\n*[[Larry Sparks]] (steel-string guitar)\n*James Alan Shelton (guitar)\n*Jack Cooke (bass)\n*John Shuffler (bass)\n*[[Lonesome Pine Fiddlers|Melvin Goins]] (bass, steel-string guitar)\n*Johnny Bonds (bass)\n*Bill Slaughter (bass)\n\n==Discography==\n\n===78 RPM===\n{| class=\"wikitable sortable\"\n!
