This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Vassar_Clements","to":"Vassar Clements"}],"pages":{"2476980":{"pageid":2476980,"ns":0,"title":"Vassar Clements","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American jazz, swing, and bluegrass Fiddler (1928\u20132005)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=October 2015}}\n{{multiple issues|\n{{Fan POV|date=August 2021}}\n{{More citations needed|date=March 2014}}\n{{More footnotes needed|date=March 2014}}}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Vassar Clements\n| image               = Vassar Clements, October 2004.gif\n| caption             = Clements during a documentary interview in 2004, Live Oak, Florida<br/>Court\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Vassar Carlton Clements\n| alias               = \n| birth_date          = {{Birth date|1928|4|25|mf=y}}\n| death_date          = {{death date and age|2005|8|16|1928|4|25}} \n| birth_place         = [[Kinards, SC]], United States\n| instrument          = [[Fiddle]], [[viola]], cello, double bass, [[mandolin]], [[tenor banjo]], guitar\n| genre               = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]], [[Country music|country]]\n| occupation          = Musician\n| years_active        = \n| label               = \n| past_member_of     = [[Bill Monroe]] and [[The Blue Grass Boys]], [[Jim and Jesse]], [[Earl Scruggs]], [[John Hartford]], [[Norman Blake (American musician)|Norman Blake]], [[Nitty Gritty Dirt Band]], [[Old & In the Way]], [[Jerry Garcia]], [[The Grateful Dead]], many others\n| website                 = \n}}\n\n'''Vassar Carlton Clements''' (April 25, 1928<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> \u2013 August 16, 2005<ref name=\"Billboard\"/>) was an American jazz, [[Swing music|swing]], and [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]] [[fiddler]]. Clements has been dubbed the Father of Hillbilly Jazz, an improvisational style that blends and borrows from swing, hot jazz, and bluegrass along with roots also in country and other musical traditions.<ref>{{cite book |last=Ledgin |first=Stephanie P. |date=2004 |title=Homegrown Music: Discovering Bluegrass|url=https://archive.org/details/homegrownmusicdi00step |url-access=registration |page=[https://archive.org/details/homegrownmusicdi00step/page/60 60]|publisher=Bloomsbury Academic |isbn=0275981150}}</ref> He was posthumously inducted into the [[International Bluegrass Music Hall of Fame]] in 2018.\n\n==Biography==\n{{more citations needed|section|date=September 2022}}\nClements was born in [[Kinard, Florida]]<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=83}}</ref> and grew up in [[Kissimmee, Florida|Kissimmee]]. He taught himself to play the fiddle at age 7, learning \"There's an Old Spinning Wheel in the Parlor\" as his first song. Soon, he joined with two first cousins, Red and Gerald, to form a local string band. In his early teens Clements met [[Bill Monroe]] and the [[Blue Grass Boys]] when they came to Florida to visit Clements' stepfather, a friend of fiddler [[Chubby Wise]]. Clements was impressed with his playing.\n\nIn late 1949, Wise left Monroe's group, and the 21 year-old Clements traveled by bus to ask for an audition. When told he would have to return the next day, Clements was crestfallen, lacking the money for either a hotel room or return bus trip. Monroe gave him some money to a night's lodging, and the next day Clements auditioned and was hired. He remained with Monroe for seven years, recording with the band in 1950 and 1951.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\nBetween 1957 and 1962, he was a member of the [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]] band [[Jim and Jesse]] & the Virginia Boys.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>  He also gained recognition joining with the popular bluegrass duo of [[Flatt and Scruggs]] on the popular theme to the hit television sitcom ''[[The Beverly Hillbillies]]''. [[Earl Scruggs]]' path-breaking banjo style had premiered with Bill Monroe in the late 1940s, and thereafter gained widespread renown with [[Lester Flatt]] and the Foggy Mountain Boys.\n\nBy the mid-1960s, however, his struggles with alcohol left him making his living in [[Blue-collar worker|blue-collar trades]], being employed briefly at the [[Kennedy Space Center]] in Florida as a plumber, in a [[Georgia (U.S. state)|Georgia]] [[paper mill]], and as switchman for [[Atlantic Coast Line Railroad]].  He even sold insurance and once operated a convenience store while owning a [[potato chip]] [[franchising|franchise]] in [[Huntsville, Alabama]]. Sobering up, he returned to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] in 1967, where he became a much sought-after studio musician.\n\nAfter a brief touring stint with [[Faron Young]] he joined [[John Hartford]]'s Dobrolic Plectral Society in 1971,<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> when he met guitarist [[Norman Blake (American musician)|Norman Blake]] and [[Dobro]] player [[Tut Taylor]], and recorded ''[[Aereo-Plain]]'', a widely acclaimed \"newgrass\" album that helped broaden the bluegrass market and sound. After less than a year he joined up with Earl Scruggs.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\nHis 1972 work with the [[Nitty Gritty Dirt Band]] on their album ''[[Will the Circle be Unbroken (Nitty Gritty Dirt Band album)|Will the Circle be Unbroken]]'' earned even wider acclaim, and he later worked on the [[Grateful Dead]]'s ''[[Wake of the Flood]]'' and [[Jimmy Buffett]]'s ''[[A White Sport Coat and a Pink Crustacean]]''.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Within the next two years, Clements would cut his first solo album.\n\nIn 1973, he joined and toured with the bluegrass supergroup [[Old & In the Way]] with [[Jerry Garcia]],<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> [[David Grisman]], [[Peter Rowan]], and [[John Kahn]]; their self-titled live album ''[[Old & In the Way (album)|Old & In the Way]]'' was released in 1975.\n[[File:Vassar Clements, Seattle, 1974.jpg|thumb|left|Clements in 1974]]\nIn 1974 he lent his talents to ''[[Highway Call]]'', a solo album by former [[Allman Brothers Band]] guitarist [[Dickey Betts]].\nHe was considered by many to be an outstanding fiddle virtuoso and he described his talent saying, {{blockquote|It was God's gift, something born in me. I was too dumb to learn it any other way. I listened to the [[Grand Ole Opry]] some. I'd pick it up one note at a time. I was young, with plenty of time and I didn't give up. You'd come home from school, do your lessons and that's it. No other distractions. I don't read music. I play what I hear.}}\n\nIn his 50-year career he played with artists ranging from [[Woody Herman]] and the Nitty Gritty Dirt Band to the Grateful Dead, [[Linda Ronstadt]], and [[Paul McCartney]], and earned at least five [[Grammy Award]] nominations and numerous professional accolades. He once recorded with the pop group [[the Monkees]] by happenstance, when he stayed behind after an earlier recording session. He also appeared in [[Robert Altman]]'s 1975 film ''[[Nashville (film)|Nashville]]''<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> and [[Alan Rudolph]]'s 1976 film, ''[[Welcome to L.A.]]''. He made a duet album with [[St\u00e9phane Grappelli]] ''Together at Last'' in 1987.\n\nIn 2004, he performed in concert with jazz quartet Third Stream \u2013 in which a video documentary of the concert was done with Jim Easton (guitar), Tom Strohman (sax), Jim Miller (bass), and John Peifer (drums).<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.vassarclements.com/tourdates_2004.html|title=Vassar Clements - Tour Dates 2004|website=Vassarclements.com|access-date=August 5, 2021}}</ref>\n\nThough he played numerous instruments, Clements indicated that he chose the fiddle over guitar recalling that, \"I picked up a guitar and fiddle and tried them both out. The guitar was pretty easy, but I couldn't get nothing out of the fiddle. So every time I'd see those instruments sitting side by side, I'd grab that fiddle.\"\n\n[[Big band]] and [[swing music]] were considerable influences upon his style and musical development, and he said that, \"Bands like [[Glenn Miller]], [[Les Brown (bandleader)|Les Brown]], [[Tommy Dorsey]], [[Harry James]] and [[Artie Shaw]] were very popular when I was a kid. I always loved rhythm, so I guess in the back of my mind the swing and jazz subconsciously comes out when I play, because when I was learning I was always trying to emulate the big-band sounds I heard on my fiddle.\"\n\nVassar Clements played on over 200 albums, including nearly 40 on which he starred or was featured. His albums often featured newgrass style music and what Clements called \"Hillbilly Jazz\". His last album, ''Livin' With the Blues'', released in 2004, was his only blues recording; it featured guest appearances by [[Elvin Bishop]], [[Norton Buffalo]], [[Maria Muldaur]], and others.\n\nHis 2005 [[Grammy Award for Best Country Instrumental Performance]] was for \"Earl's Breakdown,\" by the Nitty Gritty Dirt Band, and featured Clements, Earl Scruggs, Randy Scruggs, and [[Jerry Douglas (musician)|Jerry Douglas]].\n\nClements, whose last performance was February 4, 2005 in [[Jamestown, New York|Jamestown]], [[New York (state)|New York]], died on August 16, 2005, aged 77, of lung cancer.<ref name=\"Billboard\">{{Cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/61748/bluegrass-great-vassar-clements-dies |title=Bluegrass Great Vassar Clements Dies |date=2005-08-17 |magazine=Billboard |access-date=2019-07-13}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1507703/legendary-fiddler-vassar-clements-dead-at-age-77/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190713205822/http://www.cmt.com/news/1507703/legendary-fiddler-vassar-clements-dead-at-age-77/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=July 13, 2019 |title=Legendary Fiddler Vassar Clements Dead at Age 77 |last=Gilbert |first=Calvin |date=2005-08-16 |website=CMT News |access-date=2019-07-13}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.worldmusiccentral.org/article.php/20050817130351719 |title=World Music Central - Legendary Fiddler Vassar Clements Dies at 77 |date=2005-08-17 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20051110110716/http://www.worldmusiccentral.org/article.php/20050817130351719 |archive-date=2005-11-10 |access-date=2019-07-13}}</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n*''Southern Country Waltzes'' [[Rural Rhythm Records]] (1970)\n*''Vassar'' [[Mercury Records]] (1975)\n*''Superbow'' Mercury Records\n*''Crossing the Catskills'' (1973) Rounder Records\n*''[[Vassar Clements, John Hartford, Dave Holland]]'' (1988) [[Rounder Records]]\n*''Vassar Clements'' MCA Records\n*''The Bluegrass Session'' Flying Records\n*''Grass Routes'' Rounder Records\n*''Saturday Night Shuffle \u2013 A Celebration of Merle Travis'' Shanachie Records\n*''Hillbilly Jazz'' Flying Fish Records\n*''Hillbilly Jazz Rides Again'' (1986) Flying Fish Records   \n*''New Hillbilly Jazz'' Shikata Records\n*''Together at Last'' (Stephane Grappelli & Vassar Clements) Flying Fish Records\n*''Nashville Jam'' Flying Fish Records\n*''Westport Drive Mind'' Dust Records\n*''The Man, The Legend'' Vassillie Productions\n*''Country Classics'' Vassillie Productions\n*''Vassar Clements Reunion with Dixie Gentlemen'' Old Homestead\n*''Once in a While'' (Jam with Miles Davis' ex-band members) Flying Fish Records\n*''Live in Telluride'' (1979) Vassillie Productions\n*''Music City USA'' Vassillie Productions\n*''[[Old & In the Way (album)|Old & In the Way]]'' (1975) Rounder Records\n*''[[That High Lonesome Sound]]'' (1996) Acoustic Disc\n*''[[Breakdown (Old & In the Way album)|Breakdown]]'' (1997) Acoustic Disc\n*''[[Live at the Boarding House]]'' (2008) Acoustic Disc\n*''[[Live at the Boarding House: The Complete Shows]]'' (2013) Acoustic Disc\n*''[[The Bluegrass Sessions: Tales from the Acoustic Planet, Vol. 2]]'' (with [[B\u00e9la Fleck]]) (1999) Warner Bros. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Tony_Trischka","to":"Tony Trischka"}],"pages":{"2166584":{"pageid":2166584,"ns":0,"title":"Tony Trischka","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American five-string banjo player (born 1949)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2021}}\n{{BLP sources|date=November 2016}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name            = Tony Trischka\n| image           =\n| image_size      = 250\n| landscape       = yes\n| caption         = Tony Trischka, 2020, in his home \n| background      = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name      = Anthony Cattell Trischka\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|1949|1|16}} \n| birth_place     = [[Syracuse, New York]], U.S.\n| genre           = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]], [[country music|country]]\n| occupation      = Musician, educator\n| instrument      = Banjo\n| years_active    = 1970s\u2013present \n| label           = [[Rounder Records|Rounder]], [[Smithsonian Folkways]], Shefa Records\n| associated_acts = {{flatlist|\n*[[Skyline (band)|Skyline]]\n*[[Steve Martin]]\n*[[B\u00e9la Fleck]]\n}}\n| website         = {{URL|http://www.tonytrischka.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Anthony Cattell Trischka''' (born January 16, 1949) is an American five-string [[banjo]] player. Sandra Brennan wrote of him in 2021: \"One of the most influential modern banjoists, both in several forms of bluegrass music and occasionally in jazz and avant-garde, Tony Trischka has inspired a whole generation of progressive bluegrass musicians.\"<ref name=Brennan>{{cite web |last=Brennan |first=Sandra |work=[[AllMusic]] |date=2021 |title=Tony Trischka Biography by Sandra Brennan |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/tony-trischka-mn0000202033/biography |accessdate=2022-12-02}}</ref>\n\n==Music career==\n[[File:Bruce Molsky and Tony Trischka, New Bedford Folk Festival 2022.jpg|thumb|right|[[Bruce Molsky]] (L) and Tony Trischka at the 2022 New Bedford Folk Festival]]\nA native of Syracuse, New York, Trischka's interest in banjo was sparked by [[the Kingston Trio]]'s version of \"[[M.T.A. (song)|Charlie and the MTA]]\" in 1963. Two years later, he joined the Down City Ramblers, where he remained through 1971. That year, he made his recording debut on ''15 Bluegrass Instrumentals'' with the band Country Cooking; at the same time, he was also a member of America's premier sports-rock band Country Granola.\n\nIn 1973, he began a three-year stint with Breakfast Special. Between 1974 and 1975, he recorded two solo albums, ''Bluegrass Light'' and ''Heartlands''. Ethnomusicologist Benjamin Krakauer devotes an article to the legacy of this group in the bluegrass community, described as of ''experimental bluegrass musicians from New York City'':<ref name=\"Krakauer\">{{cite journal |last1= Krakauer|first1=Benjamin |date= Summer 2018|title=Music Scene and Its Fringes: Experimental Bluegrass of 1970s New York City |url=https://www.jstor.org/stable/10.5406/americanmusic.36.2.0163 |journal=American Music  |volume= 36|issue=2 |pages=163-193 |doi= 10.5406/americanmusic.36.2.0163|access-date=February 19, 2024}}</ref> {{Blockquote|text=Breakfast Special's innovative music incorporates jazz, avant-garde, psychedelic, klezmer, and various non- Western musical elements into their irreverent and often absurdist performances}}. This researcher explores the question of why their music has never been absorbed into the bluegrass mainstream, while the newgrass and progressive blue-grass of many of their innovative peers was widely embraced :  Benjamin Krakauer argues:<ref name=\"Krakauer\"/> {{Blockquote|text= that breakfast Special\u2019s eclecticism and related aesthetic choices made their music inaccessible to many bluegrass audiences and that the unfa-miliar aspects of this music and its presentation exacerbated conservative southern white audiences\u2019 anxieties over the performers\u2019 regional, ethnic, religious, and cultural otherness}} \nAfter one more solo album in 1976, ''Banjoland'', he went on to become musical leader for the Broadway show ''[[The Robber Bridegroom (musical)|The Robber Bridegroom]]''. Trischka toured with the show in 1978, the year he also played with the [[Monroe Doctrine]].\nIn 1978, Trischka toured Japan and recorded with [[Peter Rowan]] and [[Richard Greene (musician)|Richard Greene]]. In the early 1980s, he began recording with his group Skyline, which released its first album in 1983. Later albums included ''Robot Plane Flies over Arkansas'' (solo, 1983), ''Stranded in the Moonlight'' (with Skyline, 1984) and ''Hill Country'' (solo, 1985). In 1984, he performed in his first feature film, ''[[Foxfire (1987 film)|Foxfire]]''. Three years later, he worked on the pre-recorded music for the off-Broadway production of ''[[Driving Miss Daisy (play)|Driving Miss Daisy]]'' that featured Jessica Tandy and [[Morgan Freeman]]. Trischka produced the Belgian group Gold Rush's ''No More Angels'' in 1988. The following year, Skyline recorded its final album, ''Fire of Grace''. He also recorded the theme song for ''Books on the Air'', a popular [[National Public Radio]] show, and continued his affiliation with the network by appearing on [[Garrison Keillor]]'s ''[[Prairie Home Companion]]'', ''[[Mountain Stage]]'', ''From Our Front Porch'', and other radio shows. Trischka continued his recording career with 1993's ''World Turning'', 1995's ''Glory Shone Around: A Christmas Collection'' and 1999's ''Bend''. ''New Deal'' followed in 2003.\n\n''Double Banjo Bluegrass Spectacular'', featuring appearances by [[Steve Martin]], [[Earl Scruggs]], [[B\u00e9la Fleck]] and [[Tony Rice]], came out four years later. For this recording Trischka went back to bluegrass and reinvigorated the double banjo tradition. In October 2007, he was given an IBMA (International Bluegrass Music Association) award for Banjo Player of the Year 2007. ''Double Banjo Bluegrass Spectacular'' received IBMA awards for Recorded Event of the Year, Instrumental Album of the Year and a Grammy Nomination.\n\nHe has written over fifteen instructional books and a series of DVDs. In July 2009 he launched the groundbreaking ''Online Banjo School with Tony Trischka'', an interactive, online learning school that teaches students around the world how to play banjo with [[ArtistWorks]]. Trischka is closely associated with \"newgrass,\" which features several innovations to traditional bluegrass, including jazzy arrangements, non-traditional chordal structures, and frequent covers of non-bluegrass songs. Trischka is one of the major innovators of the \"chromatic\" banjo style, which features sinewy, snaky melodic runs not strictly played out of chord positions.\n\n2011 saw ''Give Me the Banjo'' aired on PBS stations nationwide with Trischka as the musical director and co-producer of the documentary. It was released on DVD. He produced [[Steve Martin]]'s Grammy-nominated ''Rare Bird Alert'' ([[Rounder Records|Rounder]]), which features performances by [[Paul McCartney]], the [[Dixie Chicks]] and the [[Steep Canyon Rangers]].\n\nIn December 2012, Trischka was awarded the United States Artists Friends Fellow in recognition of the excellence of his work.<ref>{{Cite web|title=United States Artists \u00bb Tony Trischka|url=https://www.unitedstatesartists.org/fellow/tony-trischka/|access-date=July 11, 2021|language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===As leader===\n* ''Bluegrass Light'' ([[Rounder Cordle"}],"pages":{"17482044":{"pageid":17482044,"ns":0,"title":"Larry Cordle","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=September 2020}}\n{{BLP sources|date=September 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = Larry Cordle\n| image            = \n| caption          = \n| background       = solo_singer\n| birth_name       = \n| alias            = \n| birth_date       = {{Birth date and age|1948|11|16}}\n| birth_place       = Eastern [[Kentucky]], U.S.\n| origin           = United States\n| instrument       = Guitar<br />vocals\n| genre            = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]]<br />[[country music|Country]]\n| occupation       = Singer-songwriter<br />musician\n| years_active     = 199x-present\n| label            = [[Sugar Hill Records (bluegrass)|Sugar Hill]], Shell Point, [[Lonesome Day Records|Lonesome Day]]\n| website          = {{URL|www.larrycordle.com}}\n| associated_acts  = [[Carl Jackson]], [[Jerry Salley]]\n}}\n'''Larry Cordle''' (born November 16, 1948) is an American [[country music|country]] and [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]] singer-songwriter\n.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/larry-cordle-mn0000124925/biography |title=Artist Biography |author=Linda Seida |publisher=allmusic.com |accessdate=September 7, 2015}}</ref> Cordle is most famous for his song \"[[Murder on Music Row]]\",<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/murder-on-music-row-mw0000625171 |author=William Ruhlmann |title=AllMusic Review |publisher=allmusic.com |accessdate=September 7, 2015 }}</ref> which was recorded by [[George Strait]] and [[Alan Jackson]] and received the [[Country Music Association]] Award for Vocal Event of the Year, and CMA nomination for Song of the Year, in 2000.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/cma-awards/2000.jhtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140114055357/http://www.cmt.com/cma-awards/2000.jhtml |url-status=dead |archive-date=January 14, 2014 |title=CMA Awards, Archive 2000 |publisher=[[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]] |access-date=September 7, 2015}}</ref>\n\n==Career==\nCordle has written songs for [[Garth Brooks]] (\"Alabama Clay\" and \"Against the Grain\", the latter of which was also recorded by [[The Oak Ridge Boys]]), [[Mountain Heart]] (\"Bitter Harvest\"), [[Ricky Skaggs]] (\"Callin' Your Name\", \"Highway 40 Blues\",  \"[[Heartbreak Hurricane]]\"), [[Loretta Lynn]] (\"Country In My Genes\"), [[George Strait]] (\"Hollywood Squares\"), [[Trisha Yearwood]] (\"Lonesome Dove\"), [[Kathy Mattea]] (\"Lonesome Standard Time\"), [[Diamond Rio]] (\"Mama, Don't Forget To Pray For Me\") and [[Bradley Walker]] (\"When I'm Hurtin'\") .\n\nCordle also has a career of his own, with his band Lonesome Standard Time. He founded the band in 1990 with his friend Glen Duncan. He received a Grammy nomination for the group's debut album, self-titled, in 1992. In 2005, Cordle's band played at the Gettysburg Bluegrass Festival. On his album 2007 \"Took Up and Put Down\", he sings \"The First Train Robbery\"; a song about the [[Reno Gang]] written from brother William Reno's perspective. The Song was written by Chris Stuart<ref>\"Gettysburg Bluegrass Festival\", ''Strings'', newsletter of the [[Pineridge Bluegrass Folklore Society]], October 2005.</ref>\n\nCordle performed on two bluegrass tribute albums for the British rock band [[the Moody Blues]]: ''[[Moody Bluegrass (musical project)|Moody Bluegrass]]: A Nashville Tribute to the Moody Blues'' (2004), and ''Moody Bluegrass TWO... Much Love'' (2011).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=4247134 |title=Moody Bluegrass: Rocking Through the Hills |publisher=NPR.org |date=December 3, 2004|accessdate=August 25, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://bluegrasstoday.com/moody-bluegrass-two%E2%80%A6much-love/ |title=Moody Bluegrass Two\u2026Much Love |publisher=bluegrasstoday.com |date=June 7, 2011 |accessdate=August 25, 2015}}</ref>\n\nAlong with friends [[Carl Jackson]] and [[Jerry Salley]], the trio (Cordle, Jackson & Salley) recorded the song \"You\u2019re Running Wild\" on the [[Louvin Brothers]] tribute on [[Universal South Records]], which features numerous country music stars singing songs made famous by the legendary duo. Entitled ''[[Livin', Lovin', Losin': Songs of the Louvin Brothers]]'', this project won the [[2004 Grammy]] for [[Grammy Award for Best Country Album|Country Album of the Year]]. The trio tours across the country and performs the hits they wrote for others.\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Larry Cordle & Lonesome Standard Time===\n* ''[[Larry Cordle, Glen Duncan & Lonesome Standard Time]]'', Sugar Hill Records (1992)\n* ''[[Murder on Music Row]]'', Shell Point Records (2000)\n* ''[[Songs from the Workbench]]'', Shell Point Records (2003)\n* ''[[Lonesome Skynyrd Time: A Bluegrass Tribute to Lynyrd Skynyrd]]'', CMH Records (2004)\n* ''[[All-Star Duets]]'', MightyCord Records (2014)\n\n===Solo===\n* ''[[Took Down and Put Up]]'' (2007)\n* ''[[Pud Marcum's Hangin']]'', MightyCord Records (2011)\n* ''[[Give Me Jesus]]'', MightyCord Records (2017)\n* ''[[Tales From East Kentucky]]'' (2018)\n* ''[[Where the Trees Know My Name]]'', MightyCord Records (2021)\n\n==References==\n{{reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [http://www.larrycordle.com Official website]\n* [{{AllMusic|class=artist|id=p33809|pure_url=yes}} Allmusic profile]\n{{CMA for Song of the Year}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Cordle, Larry}}\n[[Category:American country guitarists]]\n[[Category:American male guitarists]]\n[[Category:American country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:1949 births]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:20th-century American guitarists]]\n[[Category:20th-century American male musicians]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Kentucky]]\n[[Category:American male singer-songwriters]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. 2019|access-date=July 21, 2019}}</ref>|[[neotraditionalist country]]<ref>{{cite the Mainstream|author=Freeman, Jon|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=September 11, 2017|access-date=July 21, 2019}} [\"Skaggs had his first country Number One, at age 27, in April 1982 with the weepy ballad \u201cCrying My Heart Out Over You.\" It kicked off an incredible run of 12 chart-topping hits, placing him in the first wave of country's celebrated neotraditional movement along with George Strait, John Anderson and Randy Travis.\"]</ref>|[[gospel music|gospel]]<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1569152/ricky-skaggs-whites-record-gospel-cd/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170816203908/http://www.cmt.com/news/1569152/ricky-skaggs-whites-record-gospel-cd/|url-status=dead|archive-date=August 16, 2017|title=Ricky Skaggs, Whites Record Gospel CD|publisher=CMT.com|date=September 7, 2007|access-date=July 21, 2019}}</ref>|[[folk music|folk]]}}\n| occupation      = Singer-songwriter, [[session musician]], bandleader, producer, arranger\n| years_active    = 1961\u2013present\n| label           = [[Sugar Hill Records (bluegrass)|Sugar Hill]], [[Epic Records|Epic]], [[Rounder Records|Rounder]], DCC, [[Atlantic Records|Atlantic]], Camden, [[Rebel Records|Rebel]], [[Hollywood Records|Hollywood]], [[Legacy Records|Legacy]], Skaggs Family\n| current_member_of = [[Kentucky Thunder]]\n| spouse = {{marriage|Sharon White|1981}}\n| website         = {{URL|www.rickyskaggs.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Rickie Lee Skaggs'''<ref name=\"KT\" /><ref name=\"Excerpt from KT\">{{Cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1712490/read-from-ricky-skaggs-memoir-kentucky-traveler/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150422020630/http://www.cmt.com/news/1712490/read-from-ricky-skaggs-memoir-kentucky-traveler/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=April 22, 2015 |title=Read From Ricky Skaggs' Memoir, Kentucky Traveler |last=Skaggs |first=Ricky |date=August 16, 2013 |website=[[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]]}}</ref> (born July 18, 1954),<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.upi.com/Entertainment_News/2019/07/18/Famous-birthdays-for-July-18-Vin-Diesel-Kristen-Bell/8771563155558/|title=Famous birthdays for July 18: Vin Diesel, Kristen Bell|work=[[United Press International]]|date=July 18, 2019|access-date=August 7, 2019|archive-date=July 19, 2019|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20190719181941/https://www.upi.com/Entertainment_News/2019/07/18/Famous-birthdays-for-July-18-Vin-Diesel-Kristen-Bell/8771563155558/|url-status=live|quote=Country singer Ricky Skaggs in 1954 (age 65)}}</ref> known professionally as '''Ricky Skaggs''', is an American [[neotraditional country]] and [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]] singer, musician, producer, and [[composer]]. He primarily plays [[mandolin]]; however, he also plays [[fiddle]], guitar, [[mandocaster]], and [[banjo]].<ref name = zane>{{cite web | url = https://www.zanesvilletimesrecorder.com/story/news/local/2018/11/28/ricky-skaggs-headlining-christmas-shows/2125007002/ | publisher = Zanesville Recorder | title = Ricky Skaggs headlining Christmas shows| access-date = 2 March 2021}}</ref>\n\nSkaggs was inducted into the [[Musicians Hall of Fame and Museum]] in 2016 and both the [[International Bluegrass Music Hall of Fame]] and the [[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum|Country Music Hall of Fame]] in 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1792529/country-music-hall-of-fame-elects-ricky-skaggs-dottie-west-johnny-gimble/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180327223726/http://www.cmt.com/news/1792529/country-music-hall-of-fame-elects-ricky-skaggs-dottie-west-johnny-gimble/|url-status=dead|archive-date=March 27, 2018|title=Country Music Hall of Fame Elects Ricky Skaggs, Dottie West, Johnny Gimble|access-date=July 23, 2018}}</ref> On January 13, 2021, it was announced Skaggs had been awarded the [[National Medal of Arts]] by [[President of the United States|President]] [[Donald Trump]], alongside fellow country musician [[Toby Keith]].\n\n==Biography==\n===Early career===\nSkaggs was born in [[Cordell, Kentucky]].<ref name=\"Inc.\">{{cite book|title=American Cowboy|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=--oCAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA32|date=May\u2013June 2000|publisher=Active Interest Media, Inc.|page=32|issn=1079-3690}}</ref> He started playing music at age 5 after he was given a [[mandolin]] by his father, Hobert Skaggs. At age 6, he played mandolin and sang on stage with [[Bill Monroe]]. At age 7, he appeared on television's [[Martha White]] country music variety show, playing with [[Lester Flatt]] and [[Earl Scruggs]]. He also wanted to audition for the [[Grand Ole Opry]] at that time, but was told he was too young.\n\nIn his mid-teens, Skaggs met a fellow teen guitarist, [[Keith Whitley]], and the two started playing together with Whitley's banjo playing brother, Dwight, on radio shows. By 1970, they had earned a spot opening for [[Ralph Stanley]], and Skaggs and Keith Whitley were thereafter invited to join Stanley's band, the [[Ralph Stanley#Clinch Mountain Boys|Clinch Mountain Boys]].<ref name = pbs>{{cite web | url = https://www.pbs.org/kenburns/country-music/ricky-skaggs-biography/ | publisher = PBS | title = Ricky Skaggs Biography| access-date = 2 March 2021}}</ref>\n\nSkaggs later joined [[The Country Gentlemen]] in Washington, DC, [[J. D. Crowe]]'s [[New South (band)|New South]]. In 1976, Skaggs formed progressive bluegrass band Boone Creek, including members [[Vince Gill]] and [[Jerry Douglas]]. For a few years, Skaggs was a member of [[Emmylou Harris]]'s Hot Band. He wrote the arrangements for Harris's 1980 bluegrass-roots album, ''[[Roses in the Snow]]''. In addition to arranging for Harris, Skaggs sang harmony and played mandolin and fiddle in the Hot Band.\n\n==Country career==\nSkaggs launched his own career in 1980, achieving 12 No. 1 hits, 8 CMA awards, and 8 ACM awards. In 1982, he became a member of the [[Grand Ole Opry]], the youngest musician ever to be inducted at that time. Guitarist and producer [[Chet Atkins]] credited Skaggs with \"single-handedly\" saving country music.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.rickyskaggs.com/bio |title=The Story |publisher=Ricky Skaggs |date=July 1, 1954 |access-date=January 1, 2016 |archive-date=August 19, 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170819020842/http://www.rickyskaggs.com/bio |url-status=dead }}</ref> Skaggs is considered one of the pioneers of the [[Neotraditional country]] sub-genre.\n\nIn 1981, he debuted on [[Epic Records]] with the album ''Waitin for the Sun to Shine'', which brought him to both the country and pop charts and produced two No. 1 hits.\n\nIn 1982, he released ''[[Highways & Heartaches (Ricky Skaggs album)|Highways & Heartaches]]'', his only platinum album, featuring the instrumental heavy \"[[Highway 40 Blues]]\".\n\nKeeping with his instrumental heavy themes, he released \"[[Country Boy (Ricky Skaggs song)|Country Boy]]\" on the album of the same name. He also had [[Bill Monroe]] as a guest on this album.\n\nExploring a role as producer, Skaggs produced [[Dolly Parton]]'s album ''[[White Limozeen]]'', which started her comeback in country music.\n\nSkaggs also guested on other albums. In 1995, he sang with [[Vince Gill]] on \"[[Go Rest High on That Mountain]]\", which later won CMA's Song of the Year and was determined by [[Broadcast Music, Inc.|BMI]] to be the Most-Performed Song in 1997.\n\n==Later career==\n\nIn 1996, Skaggs went back to his [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]] roots, and also experimented with new sounds. With his band, [[Kentucky Thunder]], he is a perennial winner of Grammy Awards and International Bluegrass Music Association for best bluegrass album.\n[[File:Ricky Skaggs in May 2016 (cropped).jpg|thumb|left|Ricky Skaggs in May 2016]]\n\nIn 2000, he shared the stage with Vermont-based [[jam band]], [[Phish]].<ref>{{cite web|title=June 22, 2000 Setlist :: Phish|url=http://phish.net/setlists/?d=2000-06-22|publisher=The Mockingbird Foundation, Inc.|access-date=September 6, 2012}}</ref> On March 20, 2007, Skaggs released an album with rock musician [[Bruce Hornsby]].\n\nIn 2008, Skaggs released an album he recorded with [[The Whites]] on his Skaggs Family Records label.\n\nIn 2008, Skaggs recorded a bluegrass version of \"Old Enough\" by the [[Raconteurs]] with [[Ashley Monroe]] and the [[Raconteurs]]. He played the [[mandolin]] on the track as well as sharing vocals with [[Jack White (musician)|Jack White]], [[Brendan Benson]], and [[Ashley Monroe]].\n\nIn 2011, Skaggs, along with other musicians including the Irish band [[The Brock McGuire Band]], released their album 'Green Grass Blue Grass\", an exploration of the connection between [[Folk music of Ireland|Irish Traditional Music]] and American [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]] and [[Appalachian music]].\n\n[[File:Ricky Skaggs and Sharon White 19Aug2015.jpg|thumb|Ricky Skaggs and Sharon White, McGlohon Theater, Charlotte, NC, August 19, 2015]]\n\nAlso in 2011, Skaggs contributed to ''[[Moody Bluegrass]] TWO...Much Love'', a bluegrass [[tribute album]] to the British [[Progressive Rock]] band [[the Moody Blues]]. Skaggs sang lead vocal on the song \"[[You and Me (Moody Blues song)|You And Me]]\".<ref>\n{{cite web|title=Moody Bluegrass TWO...Much Love|url=http://www.twomuchlove.com/two-much-love-story-2/|publisher=Moody Bluegrass project website|access-date=September 6, 2015|url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150706091533/http://www.twomuchlove.com/two-much-love-story-2/|archive-date=July 6, 2015}}</ref>\n\nIn 2012, Skaggs collaborated with [[Barry Gibb]] on the song, \"Soldier's Son\" which was released on ''Music to My Ears''.\n\nIn 2015, Skaggs toured with [[Ry Cooder]], Sharon White and other members of [[The Whites]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Cozy Up To Warm Sounds for Fall with 'Cooder White Skaggs' Tour |url=http://www.rickyskaggs.com/news/09-09-15/cozy-warm-sounds-fall-cooder-white-skaggs-tour/|publisher=Ricky Skaggs website|access-date=September 9, 2015}}</ref>\n\nIn 2016, he produced the Grammy-winning album [[Love Remains (Hillary Scott album)|Love Remains]] for [[Lady Antebellum]] member [[Hillary Scott]].\n\nIn 2019, he collaborated with [[Steven Curtis Chapman]] for Chapman's album ''Deeper Roots: Where the Bluegrass Grows''\n\nIn 2019, Skaggs performed at the 6th [[Musicians Hall of Fame and Museum]] Concert and Induction Ceremony.\n\nAs of recent years, Skaggs continues performing at the historic Grand Ole Opry house in Nashville, Tennessee.\n\nIn 2021 Skaggs was nominated for the SOTE award which was delayed by the Covid pandemic.\n\n==Personal life==\nRicky Skaggs was previously married to Brenda Stanley and has two children, Andrew and Mandy, from that marriage.<ref>{{cite book|last1=Skaggs|first1=Ricky|title=Kentucky Traveler: My Life in Music|date=2014|publisher=Dey Street Books|isbn=978-0061917349}}</ref> Skaggs has been married to Sharon White of [[The Whites]] since August 1981.<ref name=\"wrightforyou.com\">{{cite web |url=http://www.wrightforyou.com/offstage2.html |title=Offstage |website=Wrightforyou.com |access-date=January 1, 2016 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160306020610/http://www.wrightforyou.com/offstage2.html |archive-date=March 6, 2016 }}</ref> They have two children; a daughter, Molly, and a son, Lucas.<ref name=\"wrightforyou.com\"/> Molly Skaggs is a Christian/Gospel singer.<ref name=\"Hallels\">{{cite web |url= http://www.hallels.com/articles/20572/20190103/listen-to-bethel-musics-new-rootsy-aint-no-grave-here.htm |title= Listen to Bethel Music's New Rootsy \"Ain't No Grave\" Here : News : Hallels |last= Yap |first= Timothy |date= January 3, 2019 |website= Hallels |access-date= December 16, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Molly Skaggs |url=https://www.cagelessbirds.com/artist-molly-skaggs |access-date=2023-08-29 |website=CAGELESS BIRDS |language=en-US}}</ref> Lucas is a multi-instrumentalist and session musician.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Luke Skaggs |url=https://www.cagelessbirds.com/artist-luke-skaggs |access-date=2023-08-29 |website=CAGELESS BIRDS |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nIn June 2020, Skaggs underwent quadruple [[coronary artery bypass graft|bypass surgery]] in Nashville.\n\nSkaggs in 2021 was awarded the National Medal of the Arts by President [[Donald Trump]].\n\n==Discography==\n{{main|Ricky Skaggs Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Lester_Flatt","to":"Lester Flatt"}],"pages":{"60626":{"pageid":60626,"ns":0,"title":"Lester Flatt","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer-songwriter (1914\u20131979)}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=June 2018}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name            = Lester Flatt\n|image           = Publicity_Photo_of_Lester_Flatt.jpg\n|image_size      = \n|caption         = Publicity Photo of Lester Flatt\n|background      = solo_singer \n|birth_name      = Lester Raymond Flatt\n|birth_date      = {{birth date|1914|6|19}}\n|birth_place     = [[Overton County, Tennessee]], U.S.\n|death_date      = {{death date and age|1979|5|11|1914|6|19}}\n|death_place     = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n|instrument      = Guitar, vocals, [[mandolin]]\n|genre           = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]], [[country music|country]]\n|occupation      = Musician, songwriter\n|years_active    = 1940\u20131979\n|label           = \n|past_member_of  = [[Flatt and Scruggs]], [[Nashville Grass]]\n}}\n\n'''Lester Raymond Flatt''' (June 19, 1914 \u2013 May 11, 1979)<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.britannica.com/biography/Lester-Flatt|title=Lester Flatt &#124; American musician|website=[[Encyclopedia Britannica]]|access-date=August 28, 2021}}</ref> was an American [[bluegrass (music)|bluegrass]] guitarist and mandolinist, best known for his collaboration with banjo picker [[Earl Scruggs]] in the duo [[Flatt and Scruggs]].\n\nFlatt's career spanned multiple decades, breaking out as a member of [[Bill Monroe]]'s band during the 1940s and including multiple solo and collaboration works exclusive of Scruggs. He first reached a mainstream audience through his performance on \"[[The Ballad of Jed Clampett]]\", the theme for the network television series ''[[The Beverly Hillbillies]]'', in the early 1960s.\n\n==Biography==\n[[File:Earl Scruggs and Lester Flatt.jpg|thumb|left|Lester Flatt (right) with [[Earl Scruggs]] (left) as part of [[Flatt and Scruggs]] in 1949]]\nFlatt was born in Duncan's Chapel, [[Overton County, Tennessee]], United States,<ref name=browne>{{cite book |editor1-last=Browne |editor1-first=Ray B. |editor2-last=Browne |editor2-first=Pat |url={{Google books|U3rJxPYT32MC|page=284|plainurl=yes}} |chapter=Flatt and Scruggs |title=The Guide to United States Popular Culture |publisher=[[Popular Press]] |year=2001 |page=284 |isbn=978-0879728212}}</ref> to Nannie Mae Haney and Isaac Columbus Flatt. In 1943, he played [[mandolin]] and sang [[tenor]] in The Kentucky Pardners, the band of [[Bill Monroe]]'s older brother [[Charlie Monroe|Charlie]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.flatt-and-scruggs.com/lesterbio.html |title=Biography: Lester Flatt |website=Flatt-and-scruggs.com |access-date=June 6, 2020}}</ref> He first came to prominence as a member of [[Bill Monroe]]'s Blue Grass Boys in 1945 and played a thumb-and-index guitar style that was in part derived from the playing of Charlie Monroe and Clyde Moody. In 1948, he started a band with fellow Monroe alumnus [[Earl Scruggs]], and for the next 20 years, [[Flatt and Scruggs]] and the Foggy Mountain Boys were one of the most successful bands in bluegrass.<ref name=ecm>{{cite book |last=Rosenberg |first=Neil V. |year=1998 |chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=tLZz02EzmBYC&pg=PT504 |chapter=Flatt & Scruggs and the Foggy Mountain Boys |title=The Encyclopedia of Country Music |publisher=Oxford University Press |pages=173\u20134 |isbn=978-0195395631}}</ref> When they parted ways in 1969, Flatt formed a new group, the [[Nashville Grass]], hiring many of the Foggy Mountain Boys. He continued to record and perform with that group until his death in 1979.<ref name=ecm2>{{cite book |last=Samuelson |first=Dave |year=1998 |chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=tLZz02EzmBYC&pg=PT504 |chapter=Lester Flatt & the Nashville Grass |title= The Encyclopedia of Country Music |editor-first=Paul |editor-last=Kingsbury |location=New York |publisher=Oxford University Press |page=173 |isbn=978-0195395631}}</ref> His role as rhythm guitarist and vocalist in each of these seminal ensembles helped define the sound of traditional bluegrass music. His solid guitar playing and rich lead voice are unmistakable in hundreds of bluegrass standards. He is also remembered for his library of compositions.\n\n==Death and legacy==\nFlatt died of heart failure in Nashville, Tennessee, at the age of 64.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/1979/05/12/archives/lester-flatt-singer-and-guitarist-in-duo-with-earl-scruggs-dies.html |title=Lester Flatt, Singer and Guitarist in Duo With Earl Scruggs, Dies |first=John |last=Rockwell |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |page=26 |date=May 12, 1979}}</ref>\n\nHe was posthumously inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame]] in 1985 along with Scruggs.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://countrymusichalloffame.org/Inductees/InducteeDetail/flatt-and-scruggs |title=Flatt and Scruggs |website=[[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum]] |access-date=August 15, 2016}}</ref> Flatt was also posthumously inducted as an inaugural member of the [[International Bluegrass Music Hall of Honor]] in 1991.\n\nLester's hometown of [[Sparta, Tennessee]], held a bluegrass festival in his honor for a number of years, before being discontinued a few years prior to the death of the traditional host, resident Everette Paul England; Lester Flatt Memorial Bluegrass Day remains part of the annual Liberty Square Celebration held in Sparta.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.eastpublicrelations.com/lester_flatt_memorial_bluegrass.htm |title=Lester Flatt Memorial Bluegrass Day |website=East Public Relations |date=September 29, 2007 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071205192520/http://www.eastpublicrelations.com/lester_flatt_memorial_bluegrass.htm |archive-date=December 5, 2007 |df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\nFlatt and Scruggs were ranked No. 24 on [[Country Music Television|CMT]]'s 40 Greatest Men of Country Music in 2003.\n\n==Discography==\n[[File:Lester-flatt-sparta-tn-memorial2.jpg|right|thumb|Lester Flatt memorial in Sparta, Tennessee]]\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Tony_Furtado","to":"Tony Furtado"}],"pages":{"1655061":{"pageid":1655061,"ns":0,"title":"Tony Furtado","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name            = Tony Furtado\n| image           = Tony Furtado Fox Theatre Boulder CO February 2008.jpg\n| image_size    = \n| landscape      = \n| caption          = Fox Theater, Boulder, Colorado, February 8, 2008\n| background    = solo_singer\n| birth_name    = \n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|mf=y|1967|10|18}}\n| birth_place     = [[Pleasanton, California]], U.S.\n| genre            = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]], [[country music|country]], [[rock music|rock]]\n| occupation     = Musician\n| instrument     =  [[banjo]], [[slide guitar]], [[electric guitar]]\n| years_active  =\n| label             = [[Rounder Records|Rounder]], Yousay Furtado Records\n| associated_acts =\n| website      = {{URL|www.tonyfurtado.com}}\n}}\n'''Tony Furtado''' (born October 18, 1967) is an American singer-songwriter, banjoist, and guitarist.\n\n== History ==\n[[Image:Tony Furtado 2.jpg|left|thumb|Fox Theater, Boulder, Colorado, February 8, 2008]]\nFurtado was born in [[Pleasanton, California]]. He took up the banjo at age 12, inspired by the [[The Beverly Hillbillies|Beverly Hillbillies]] television show and a sixth-grade music report. He studied music and art at [[California State University, East Bay|California State, Hayward]]. He first attracted national attention in 1987, when he won the National Bluegrass Banjo Championship in Winfield, Kansas. Then he toured with bluegrass musician [[Laurie Lewis]]. [[Rounder Records]] released his debut album, ''Swamped'', in 1990.<ref>[http://www.modernguitars.com/archives/002779.html \"Tony Furtado Interview\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070501142050/http://www.modernguitars.com/archives/002779.html |date=2007-05-01 }} by Tom Watson, January 18, 2007 ''Modern Guitars''.</ref>\n\nIn 1990, Tony signed a recording deal with [[Rounder Records]], one of the country's preeminent independent record companies. Beginning with Swamped in 1990, he recorded six critically acclaimed albums for the label, collaborating with such master musicians as [[Alison Krauss]], [[Jerry Douglas]], [[Tim O'Brien (musician)|Tim O'Brien]], [[Stuart Duncan]], [[Kelly Joe Phelps]] and [[Mike Marshall (musician)|Mike Marshall]]. During this period, Tony also performed and recorded with the band SugarBeat and the Rounder Banjo Extravaganza with [[Tony Trischka]] and Tom Adams.\n\nBeginning in the late 1990s \u2013 influenced by such musicians as [[Ry Cooder]], [[David Lindley (musician)|David Lindley]] and [[Taj Mahal (musician)|Taj Mahal]] \u2013 Tony added slide guitar, singing and songwriting to his musical toolbox and began leading his own band.\n\nFurtado is an accomplished sculptor.\n\n== Performance ==\nFurtado is a tireless road musician who performs in a variety of formats: solo, in a duo, or trio or with his full five-person band. He has toured with such legendary musicians as [[Gregg Allman]] and with such esteemed slide guitarists as David Lindley, Derek Trucks, and [[Sonny Landreth]].\n\nHe has performed throughout the world at top venues and appeared at such prestigious music festivals as the [[Telluride Bluegrass Festival]], High Sierra Music Festival, Jazz Aspen, Kerrville Folk Festival, Strawberry Music Festival, Winnipeg Folk Festival, Sisters Folk Festival, San Jose Jazz Festival and countless others. . His second album, ''Within Reach'' (1992), featured bluegrass veterans [[Alison Krauss]] and [[Jerry Douglas]].\n\nHe recorded a duet album with [[Dirk Powell]].<ref name=\"Wilson\">{{cite web|last1=Wilson|first1=MacKenzie|title=Tony Furtado {{!}} Biography & History {{!}} AllMusic|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/tony-furtado-mn0000000589/biography|website=AllMusic|accessdate=29 October 2016}}</ref>\n\n== Band ==\nHis band Sugarbeat also featured Ben Demerath (vocals, guitar), [[Matt Flinner]] (mandolin), and Sally Truitt (bass).<ref name=\"TF-deseret-1994\">{{cite news|last1=Bonham|first1=Nicole A.|title=Sugarbeat Reels In Audience with Songs about Fish, Future|url=http://www.deseretnews.com/article/337882/SUGARBEAT-REELS-IN-AUDIENCE-WITH-SONGS-ABOUT-FISH-FUTURE.html?pg=all|accessdate=August 6, 2017|work=Deseret News|date=February 21, 1994}}</ref>\n\n==Awards and honors ==\n* Won [[National Bluegrass Banjo Championship]], [[Winfield, Kansas]], 1987 and 1991\n\n==Musical style==\nTony is an evocative and soulful singer, a wide-ranging songwriter and a virtuoso multi-instrumental-ist adept on banjo, cello-banjo, slide guitar and baritone ukulele who mixes and matches sounds and styles with the flair of a master chef.  Comparisons to [[Ry Cooder]] were rooted in Furtado's combination of jazz, Celtic, and old-time music. On his third album, ''Full Circle'' (1994) he concentrated on acoustic blues and [[slide guitar]], with Cooder as an influence.\n\n\"Furtado mixes Americana, folk, indie-rock, blues, and jazz styles.\"<ref>[http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/article.asp?xid=1001 \"Tony Furtado goes for a lucky 'Thirteen'\"] by Jason MacNeil, January 2007, ''Country Standard Time''</ref>\n\n\"As a banjo virtuoso, Furtado is well known for his envelope-pushing, progressive bluegrass stylings. His picking is rapid-fire quick, sharp and clear, and puts him in the school of B\u00e9la Fleck and [[David Grisman]].\"<ref>[http://www.telluridegateway.com/articles/2007/03/09/the_pulse/pulse03.txt \"Furtado brings eclectic bag of tricks to Opera House\"] by Katie Klingsporn, March 8, 2007, ''Telluride Daily Planet''.</ref>\n\n\"He mixes bluegrass roots with a mainstream pop streak, easily holding the spotlight, thanks to his restrained virtuosity on acoustic and slide guitar and a warmly engaging voice reminiscent of T Bone Burnett, sans preachiness. \u2013 ''Paste'' magazine\n\n== This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Devil_Makes_Three_(band)","to":"The Devil Makes Three (band)"}],"pages":{"7850608":{"pageid":7850608,"ns":0,"title":"The Devil Makes Three (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American bluegrass trio from Santa Cruz, California}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = The Devil Makes Three\n| background       = group_or_band\n| image            = The Devil Makes Three 2016.jpg\n| image_size       = \n| caption          = The Devil Makes Three in 2016\n| alias            = \n| origin           = [[Santa Cruz, California|Santa Cruz]], [[California]]\n| genre            = {{flatlist|\n*[[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]]\n*[[Americana (music)|Americana]]\n*[[Folk music|folk]]\n*[[folk blues]]\n*[[old-time music|old-time]]\n*[[Country music|country]]\n}}\n| years_active     = 2002\u2013present\n| label            = {{flatlist|\n*[[Milan Records|Milan]]\n*[[New West Records|New West]]\n*[[Monkeywrench Records|Monkeywrench]]\n*Khan\n}}\n| associated_acts  = \n| website          = {{URL|http://thedevilmakesthree.com}}\n| current_members  = Pete Bernhard<br />Lucia Turino<br />Cooper McBean\n| past_members     = \n}}\n'''The Devil Makes Three''' is an [[Americana (music)|Americana]] band from [[Santa Cruz, California]], United States.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://amusicblogyea.com/2015/03/17/gimme-your-answers-an-interview-w-the-devil-makes-three/|title=Gimme Your Answers: An Interview w/ The Devil Makes Three|last=Fox|first=Iain|date=17 March 2015|website=Amusicblogyea.com|access-date=22 September 2016}}</ref> The group blends [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]], [[old time music|old time]], [[country music|country]], [[folk music|folk]], [[blues music|blues]], [[jazz music|jazz]], and [[ragtime music|ragtime]] music.<ref name=\"bio\">{{cite web|url=http://www.thedevilmakesthree.com/biography.php|title=Biography - The Devil Makes Three|publisher=Milan Records|accessdate=14 July 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090820183835/http://thedevilmakesthree.com/biography.php|archive-date=20 August 2009|url-status=dead}}</ref> The group's members are [[guitarist]] Pete Bernhard, [[Double bass|upright bassist]] Lucia Turino, and [[guitarist]] and [[banjo|tenor banjo]] player Cooper McBean.\n\n==Career==\nThe band has released six full-length albums.  They independently released a self-titled album in 2002.  Another independent release followed in 2004, ''Longjohns, Boots, And A Belt''.  The band recorded two shows in April 2006 in [[Felton, California|Felton]], [[California]] with guest [[fiddle]]r Chojo Jacques.  The recordings were later released as a live album, ''A Little Bit Faster And A Little Bit Worse''.\n\nAfter the release of their live album, the band signed with independent label [[Milan Records]], which specializes in [[film scores]] and [[soundtrack]]s.  Their first album on Milan was a re-release of their debut album, ''The Devil Makes Three''.  In 2009, they followed with an all-new album, ''Do Wrong Right''.\n\nBand member Bernhard independently released a solo album, ''Things I Left Behind'' (2006).  In September 2009 Bernhard released his next solo album, ''Straight Line'', on Milan Records.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.antimusic.com/news/09/june/30The_Devil_Makes_Three_Frontman_Goes_Solo_Again.shtml|title=The Devil Makes Three Frontman Goes Solo Again|date=30 June 2009|website=Antimusic.com|accessdate=17 July 2009}}</ref>\n\nMcBean and Bernhard are originally from near Brattleboro, Vermont, where they played music together as childhood friends and when they were in high school.  They were also acquainted with Turino (from New Hampshire but raised in Vermont), but didn't know her well.  After graduating from high school, all three moved to California separately, Bernhard by way of Nashville.  Bernhard and McBean re-connected in Olympia.  Later in Santa Cruz they also became reacquainted with Turino, forming the band soon after in 2001.<ref name=\"auto\">{{cite web|last1=Linn|first1=Sarah|title=The Devil Makes Three ready to rock at SLO concert|url=http://www.sanluisobispo.com/entertainment/music-news-reviews/article39510666.html|website=The Tribune (San Luis Obispo)|accessdate=14 January 2018|date=28 January 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Jasper|first1=David|title=Hillbilly punk: The Devil Makes Three has unplugged and gone country|url=http://www.bendbulletin.com/slideshows/1506523-151/hillbilly-punk|website=The Bulletin|accessdate=14 January 2018|date=14 April 2006}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Fun Has Just Begun: The Devil Makes Three comes home thirsty and ready to rock|url=http://goodtimes.sc/uncategorized/fun-has-just-begun/|website=Goodtimes.sc|accessdate=14 January 2018|date=27 December 2011}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Ellis|first1=Lauren|title=Doing Wrong Right: The Devil Makes Three|url=https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2011/10/the-devil-makes-three-stomp-and-smash/|website=Mother Jones|accessdate=14 January 2018|date=31 October 2011}}</ref><ref name=\"auto1\">{{cite web|last1=Peterson|first1=Kate|title=Devil's in the Details|url=http://inweekly.net/wordpress/?p=9993|website=In Weekly |accessdate=14 January 2018|date=16 May 2012}}</ref>  Before forming The Devil Makes Three with Turino, both Bernhard and McBean played in punk bands and later toured as a duo.<ref name=\"charleston\">{{cite web |last1=Lawrence |first1=Stratton |title=Moshing with folk-punk act the Devil Makes Three |url=https://www.charlestoncitypaper.com/charleston/moshing-with-folk-punk-act-the-devil-makes-three/Content?oid=3654375 |website=Charleston City Paper |accessdate=4 September 2018 |date=3 December 2011}}</ref>\n\nAround 2010, Bernhard and Turino moved back to Brattleboro. McBean remained in California and later moved to Austin.<ref name=\"auto\"/><ref>{{cite web|last1=Diamond|first1=Austen|title=The Devil Makes Three Tonight at the State Room: Americana band The Devil Makes Three farms for forbidden fruit.|url=https://www.cityweekly.net/utah/the-devil-makes-three/Content?oid=2149729|website=Salt Lake City Weekly|accessdate=14 January 2018|date=10 October 2010}}</ref><ref name=\"auto1\"/> Despite no longer living in the same town, the band continues to tour and write.\n\nIn August 2010, the band performed at [[Outside Lands Music and Arts Festival]]. They have also performed several times at the annual [[Hardly Strictly Bluegrass]] Festival.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.sfstation.com/2013/10/01/devil-makes-three-hardly-strictly-bluegrass/|title=Devil Makes Three Returns With New Music to Hardly Strictly Bluegrass|website=Sfstation.com|accessdate=22 August 2018}}</ref>\n\nOn June 4, 2018, The Devil Makes Three announced their new studio album, ''[[Chains Are Broken]]'', which was produced by [[Ted Hutt]] and released on August 24, 2018, via [[New West Records]]. Along with the album announcement, they released \"Paint My Face\" as a streaming single and released another album track, \"Bad Idea\", on July 13, 2018.\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Whites","to":"The Whites"}],"pages":{"6698751":{"pageid":6698751,"ns":0,"title":"The Whites","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country and gospel band}}\n{{about|the American musical group|the Russian political movement known as the Whites|White movement|other uses|White (disambiguation)}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = The Whites\n| image            = TheWhites.jpg\n| caption          = The Whites performing on August 8, 2008.\n| image_size       = \n| background       = group_or_band\n| alias            = \n| origin           = [[Fort Worth, Texas]], United States<br/>[[Nashville, Tennessee]], United States\n| genre            = {{Hlist|[[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]]|[[Gospel music|Gospel]]|[[Country music|Country]]}}\n| years_active     = 1972&ndash;present\n| label            = [[Curb Records|Curb]], [[Warner Records|Warner Bros.]], [[MCA Records|MCA]], Ridge Runner, [[Word Records|Word]], [[EOne Music|Koch]], Skaggs Family\n| current_members  = Buck White<br>Sharon White<br>Cheryl White\n}}\n\n'''The Whites''' are an American [[country music]] vocal group from [[Fort Worth, Texas]], United States. They consist of sisters Sharon White and Cheryl White, and their father, Buck White. Sharon plays guitar, Cheryl is the bassist and Buck plays the mandolin. Formed in 1972, the trio has recorded multiple albums and charted multiple songs on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] chart. They are also known as frequent collaborators of country and bluegrass musician [[Ricky Skaggs]], who is Sharon's husband.\n\n==Overview==\nThe Whites consist of Sharon White (born December 17, 1953), her sister Cheryl (born January 27, 1955), and their father Buck (born December 13, 1930).<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=442/3}}</ref> Buck grew up playing music and started playing in dances wrestling arenas, auditoriums but he didn't really like that atmosphere a lot.<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite news |last=Weintraub |first=Boris |date=November 1981 |title=Buck White and the Down Home Folks |pages=9-13 |work=Bluegrass Unlimited}}</ref> Buck had two jobs when the sisters were growing up; a plumber by day, piano and mandolin player by night.<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite book |last=Henry |first=Murphy Hicks |title=Pretty Good for a Girl: Women in Bluegrass |publisher=University of Illinois |year=2013 |isbn=9780252095887 |pages=157-159}}</ref> He started really enjoying music when his family started playing together all around the world. In the beginning, Sharon took up bass when she was twelve, moving to guitar when Cheryl took over on bass.<ref name=\":0\" /> \n\nIn the 1980s, they scored such hits as \"You Put The Blue In Me\", \"Hangin' Around\", \"Give Me Back That Old Familiar Feeling\", \"Pins And Needles\", \"If It Ain't Love (Let's Leave It Alone)\", \"Hometown Gossip\", and \"When The New Wears Off of Our Love\".<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\nIn August 1981,<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.wrightforyou.com/offstage2.html|title=Offstage|date=March 6, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160306020610/http://www.wrightforyou.com/offstage2.html|access-date=August 11, 2021|archive-date=2016-03-06}}</ref> Sharon White married [[Ricky Skaggs]], who performed on several of the Whites' early releases.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> In 1987, the couple released the hit song, \"Love Can't Ever Get Better Than This\".\n\nIn 1991, the Whites joined producers [[Randall Franks]] and [[Alan Autry]] on the ''[[In the Heat of the Night (TV Series)|In The Heat Of The Night]]'' TV series album entitled ''Christmas Time's A Comin''', performing on the track, \"Let's Live Everyday Like It Was Christmas\" (Sonlite/MGM/UA).\n\nThe Whites became members of the [[Grand Ole Opry]] in 1984 and were current regulars on the program in [[Nashville, Tennessee]].  Their collaborative album with Ricky Skaggs, \"Salt of the Earth\" won the 2008 [[Grammy]] for Best Southern/Country/Bluegrass Album.\n\nThe Whites can be heard on the [[O Brother, Where Art Thou? (soundtrack)|''O Brother, Where Art Thou?'' soundtrack]] with the song \"[[Keep on the Sunny Side]]\". They also appear in ''[[Down from the Mountain]]'', the documentary of a concert given by the soundtrack artists.<ref name=\":0\" />\n\nThe Whites were inducted into the [[Texas Country Music Hall of Fame]] on Saturday, August 16, 2008, in [[Carthage, Texas]].  They were inducted along with [[Buck Owens]] and [[Mickey Newbury]].\n\nAlso performing on the Grand Ole Opry with Buck, Sharon and Cheryl is Rosanna, better known as Rosie, the third of the four White sisters. She performs high harmony and occasionally does solo performance of the Mel Tillis classic \"The Violet and the Rose\".\n\n==Awards and nominations==\nThe Whites have been nominated for five [[CMA Awards]] (The Horizon/New Artist award 1983, Vocal Group of the Year 1983/1985 and Instrumental Group of the Year 1983/1985) and won the Album of the Year honour in 2001 for their contribution to \"[[O Brother, Where Art Thou? (soundtrack)|O Brother, Where Art Thou?]]\". In 1987, Sharon White and her husband Ricky Skaggs won the Vocal Duo of the Year award.\n\nThey also received Top Vocal Group nominations in 1982 and 1983 from the [[ACM Awards]] and an album of the year nomination for \"O Brother, Where Art Thou?\".<ref name=\":1\" />\n\nIn 1984, they were inducted into the [[Grand Ole Opry]].\n\nIn 1987, Sharon White and her husband [[Ricky Skaggs]] won the [[Country Music Association Award for Vocal Duo of the Year]].\n\nAlso for their contribution to \"O Brother, Where Art Thou?\", The Whites won Album of the Year at the 2001 [[International Bluegrass Music Awards]]. That same year, Sharon and Cheryl also received the Recorded Event of the Year award for their contribution to \"Follow Me Back to the Fold: A Tribute to Women in Bluegrass\". In 2006, they were awarded the IBMA's Distinguished Achievement Award for their contributions to the genre.\n\nThe Whites were among the artists honoured with the prestigious [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year]] for \"O Brother, Where Art Thou?\". [[Salt of the Earth (Ricky Skaggs & The Whites album)|Salt of the Earth]], their 2007 collaboration with Ricky Skaggs won them a [[Grammy Award for Best Southern, Country or Bluegrass Gospel Album]].\n\nIn 2007, The Whites and Ricky Skaggs received a [[GMA Dove Awards of 2007|GMA Dove Award]] for Bluegrass Recorded Album of the Year.\n\nIn 2008, they were inducted into the [[Texas Country Music Hall of Fame]].\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:22em;\"| Title\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Album details\n! colspan=\"2\"| Peak positions\n|- style=\"font-size:smaller;\"\n! width=\"45\"| [[Top Country Albums|US Country]]\n! width=\"45\"| [[Top Bluegrass Albums|US Grass]]\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Buck White & the Down Home Folks''<br>{{small|(as Buck White & the Down Home Folks)}}\n| \n* Release date: 1972\n* Label: County Records\n| \u2014\n| \u2014\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''In Person''<br>{{small|(as Buck White & the Down Home Folks)}}\n| \n* Release date: 1977\n* Label: County Records\n| \u2014\n| \u2014\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''That Down Home Feeling''<br>{{small|(as Buck White & the Down Home Folks)}}\n| \n* Release date: 1977\n* Label: [[Ridge Runner Records]]\n| \u2014\n| \u2014\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Poor Folks' Pleasure''<br>{{small|(as Buck White & the Down Home Folks)}}\n| \n* Release date: 1978\n* Label: [[Sugar Hill Records (bluegrass label)|Sugar Hill Records]]\n| \u2014\n| \u2014\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''More Pretty Girls Than One''<br>{{small|(Buck White solo)}}\n| \n* Release date: 1979\n* Label: Sugar Hill Records\n| \u2014\n| \u2014\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Old Familiar Feeling''\n| \n* Release date: June 1983\n* Label: [[Curb Records|Curb]] / [[Warner Bros.
