This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Alison_Krauss","to":"Alison Krauss"}],"pages":{"466275":{"pageid":466275,"ns":0,"title":"Alison Krauss","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American musician (b. 1971)}}\n{{About|the bluegrass musician|the Kent State student|Allison Krause}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Alison Krauss\n| image             = Alison Krauss MerleFest 2007 01.jpg\n| image_upright     = 1.2\n| caption           = Krauss at the 2007 [[MerleFest]]\n| birth_name        = Alison Maria Krauss\n| birth_date        = {{birth date and age|mf=yes|1971|7|23}}\n| birth_place       = [[Decatur, Illinois]], U.S.\n| origin            = [[Champaign, Illinois]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{hlist|[[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]]|[[Country music|country]]|[[Pop music|pop]]}}\n| occupation        = Musician\n| instrument        = {{hlist|Vocals|[[fiddle]]|[[piano]]|[[mandolin]]}}\n| years_active      = 1984\u2013present\n| label             = {{hlist|[[Rounder Records|Rounder]]|[[Capitol Records|Capitol]]}}\n| current_member_of = {{flatlist|\n*[[Alison Krauss & Union Station]]\n*[[Robert Plant]] and Alison Krauss<ref>{{Cite web |date=2023-01-31 |title=Robert Plant and Alison Krauss Reveal 2023 North American Tour Dates |url=https://relix.com/news/detail/robert-plant-and-alison-krauss-reveal-2023-north-american-tour-dates/ |access-date=2023-02-11 |website=Relix Media |language=en-US}}</ref>\n}}\n| spouse            = {{marriage|[[Pat Bergeson]]|1997|2001|reason=divorced}}\n| website           = {{URL|alisonkrauss.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Alison Maria Krauss''' (born July 23, 1971) is an American [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]]-[[Country music|country]] singer, [[fiddler]] and producer. She entered the [[music of the United States|music industry]] at an early age, competing in local contests by the age of eight and recording for the first time at 14. She signed with [[Rounder Records]] in 1985 and released her first solo album in 1987. She was invited to join [[Alison Krauss and Union Station|Union Station]], releasing her first album with them as a group in 1989 and performing with them ever since.<ref name=AllMusic>{{cite web|url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/alison-krauss-mn0000745071/biography |title=Alison Krauss Biography |last=Erlewine |first=Stephen Thomas |author-link=Stephen Thomas Erlewine |website=[[AllMusic]] |access-date=December 6, 2020}}</ref>\n\nKrauss has released 14 albums, appeared on numerous soundtracks, and sparked a renewed interest in bluegrass music in the United States. Her soundtrack performances have led to further popularity, including the [[O Brother, Where Art Thou? (soundtrack)|''O Brother, Where Art Thou?'' soundtrack]], and the [[Cold Mountain (soundtrack)|''Cold Mountain'' soundtrack]], which led to her performance at the [[76th Academy Awards|2004 Academy Awards]]. Platinum-selling ''[[Raising Sand]]'' (2007) was the first of her two collaborations with English rock singer [[Robert Plant]].\n\nAs of 2019, she has won 27 [[Grammy Award]]s from 42 nominations,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/artists/alison-krauss/16961 |title=Artist: Alison Krauss |date=November 23, 2020 |publisher=[[Grammy Awards]] |access-date=December 6, 2020}}</ref> ranking her [[Grammy Award records#Most Grammys won|fourth]] behind [[Beyonc\u00e9]], [[Quincy Jones]] and classical conductor [[Georg Solti]] for most Grammy Award wins overall.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/music-news/9078641/Alison-Krauss-makes-Grammy-history.html |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220111/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/music-news/9078641/Alison-Krauss-makes-Grammy-history.html |archive-date=January 11, 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live|title=Alison Krauss makes Grammy history|date=February 13, 2012|newspaper=[[The Daily Telegraph]]|author=Martin Chilton}}{{cbignore}}</ref> Krauss was the singer and female artist with the most awards in Grammy history<ref name=\"Grammys\">{{cite news|title=Plant, Krauss rise with 'Raising Sand' at Grammys|url=http://www.cnn.com/2009/SHOWBIZ/Music/02/08/grammy.night/index.html |publisher=CNN|first=Ted|last=Leopold|date=February 9, 2009|access-date=July 27, 2009}}</ref> until Beyonc\u00e9 won her 28th Grammy in [[63rd Annual Grammy Awards|2021]].<ref>{{cite news |last=Exposito |first=Suzy |date=March 14, 2021 |title=Beyonc\u00e9 breaks record for most Grammys by a female artist |url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/music/story/2021-03-14/beyonce-breaks-record-grammys-female-artist |work=Los Angeles Times |access-date=March 19, 2021}}</ref> When Krauss won her first Grammy in [[33rd Annual Grammy Awards|1991]], she was the second-youngest winner at that time.\n\nOn November 21, 2019, she was awarded the [[List of recipients of the National Medal of Arts|National Medal of Arts]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=President Donald J. Trump to Award the National Medal of Arts and National Humanities Medal |via=[[NARA|National Archives]] |work=[[whitehouse.gov]] |url=https://trumpwhitehouse.archives.gov/briefings-statements/president-donald-j-trump-award-national-medal-arts-national-humanities-medal/ |access-date=November 21, 2019}}</ref> She was inducted into the [[International Bluegrass Music Hall of Fame]] in September 2021.<ref name=\"Rogers\">{{cite news |last=Rogers |first=Steve |date=July 22, 2021 |title=Bluegrass Hall of Fame inductees for 2021 announced |url=https://www.wtvq.com/2021/07/22/bluegrass-hall-of-fame-inductees-for-2021-announced/ |publisher=WTVQ |location=Lexington, Kentucky |access-date=July 23, 2021}}</ref>\n\n==Early life==\nAlison Maria Krauss<ref>[http://repertoire.bmi.com/writer.asp?page=1&blnWriter=True&blnPublisher=True&blnArtist=True&fromrow=1&torow=25&affiliation=BMI&cae=230502523&keyID=384922&keyname=KRAUSS%20ALISON%20MARIA&querytype=WriterID \"Songwriter/Composer: Krauss, Alison Maria\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151019090122/http://repertoire.bmi.com/writer.asp?page=1&blnWriter=True&blnPublisher=True&blnArtist=True&fromrow=1&torow=25&affiliation=BMI&cae=230502523&keyID=384922&keyname=KRAUSS%20ALISON%20MARIA&querytype=WriterID |date=October 19, 2015 }}. [[Broadcast Music, Inc.|BMI]] Repertoire Search.</ref> was born in [[Decatur, Illinois]],<ref>{{cite news |title=Decatur Births |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/64747923/decatur-births/ |work=Decatur Herald |location=Decatur, Illinois |date=July 27, 1971 |page=24 |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref><ref name=\"Macnie2004\">{{cite book|last=Macnie|first=Jim|editor=Thomas Goldsmith|title=The Bluegrass Reader|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=LgAGzopOTbYC&pg=PA277|year=2004|publisher=University of Illinois Press|isbn=978-0-252-02914-1|page=277}}</ref>{{Ref label|ida|a|none}} to Fred and Louise Krauss. \n\nFred Krauss was a German immigrant who came to the United States in 1952 at age 12, and taught his native language while he earned a doctorate in [[psychology]]. He later went into the business of [[real estate]]; among the properties he owned was the so-called [[American Football House]], located at 704 W. High St. in [[Urbana, Illinois|Urbana]], which was featured on the cover of [[American Football (1999 album)|the first album]] by [[emo]] band [[American Football (band)|American Football]].<ref>{{cite web |title=History |url=https://www.americanfootball.house/history |website=americanfootball.house |access-date=26 August 2024}}</ref> Louise Krauss, an American of German and Italian descent, is the daughter of artists, and works as an [[illustrator]] of magazines and textbooks.<ref name=Argus1985>{{cite news |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/64737367/teenage-girl-fiddling-up-a-storm/ |title=Teen girl fiddling up a storm in musician meets |date=July 21, 1985 |agency=[[Associated Press]] |newspaper=[[The Dispatch / The Rock Island Argus|The Argus]] |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref> Fred and Louise met while they were studying at the [[University of Illinois at Urbana\u2013Champaign]].<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=tQ0EAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA3 |title=Alison Krauss: An Unforgettable Force |date=June 5, 1999 |last=White |first=Timothy |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |page=3 |volume=111 |number=23 |issn=0006-2510 }}</ref> \n\nAfter a brief residence in nearby Decatur, the family settled in [[Champaign, Illinois|Champaign]], where Krauss was raised with her older brother, [[Viktor Krauss|Viktor]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://bluegrassmusic.com/content/2011/feature/alison-krauss-union-station/ |title=Alison Krauss + Union Station Flight Plan: Paper Airplane Lands AKUS Back On The Bus \u00ab Bluegrass Unlimited Bluegrass Unlimited |website=Bluegrassmusic.com |date=October 2, 2011 |access-date=July 1, 2013 |archive-date=August 1, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130801024005/http://bluegrassmusic.com/content/2011/feature/alison-krauss-union-station/ |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\nKrauss's mother played [[banjo]] and [[acoustic guitar]],<ref name=Argus1985/> so Krauss was exposed to [[folk music]] at home, and she heard [[Rock music|rock]] and [[pop music]] on the radio: She liked [[Gary Numan]]'s [[synth-pop]] song \"[[Cars (song)|Cars]]\", and rock bands such as [[Foreigner (band)|Foreigner]], [[Bad Company]], and [[Electric Light Orchestra]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/entertainment-arts-39256295 |title=Alison Krauss reacts to Beyonce's Grammy 'threat' |date=March 15, 2017 |last=Savage |first=Mark |newspaper=[[BBC News]] |access-date=December 6, 2020}}</ref> Her brother Viktor played  [[piano]] and [[double bass]] in high school, launching a career as a [[jazz]] and rock multi-instrumentalist.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/63542244/back-to-her-roots/ |title=Back to Her Roots |last=Craft |first=Dan |date=October 13, 2005 |newspaper=[[The Pantagraph]] |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref> At her mother's insistence, Krauss began studying [[classical music|classical]] violin at age five.<ref name=Thomas1990/> Krauss was reluctant to spend time practicing, but she continued with classical lessons until she was eleven.<ref name=Graybill1984/> Krauss said her mother \"tried to find interesting things for me to do\" and \"wanted to get me involved in music, in addition to art and sports\".<ref name=\"gac1\">[https://archive.today/20130124075823/http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_music_beat/article/0,3034,GAC_26067_4785799_,00.html \"Alison Krauss Keeps Her Pace After Quick Start\"] by Ronna Rubin for ''GAC Music Beat'', Great American Country, June 19, 2006. Retrieved June 28, 2006.</ref> Krauss was also very active in [[roller skating]], and in her teens she finally decided on a career in music rather than [[roller derby]].<ref name=Thomas1990>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/archive/lifestyle/style/1990/08/19/not-just-fiddling-around/cd919f1b-e079-4453-aa73-d4cccb3e0a6d/ |title=Not Just Fiddling Around |date=August 19, 1990 |last=Thomas |first=Dana |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |access-date=December 6, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/64746934/alison-krauss-chose-music-over-roller/ |title=Alison Krauss chose music over roller derby |date=January 2, 1991 |last=Edwards |first=Joe |agency=[[Associated Press]] |newspaper=Journal Gazette |location=[[Mattoon, Illinois]] |page=7 |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref>\n\nIn mid-1979, Krauss's mother saw a notice for an upcoming fiddle competition at the Champaign County Fair, so she bought a [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]] fiddle instruction book and the 1977 bluegrass album ''Duets'' by violinist [[Richard Greene (musician)|Richard Greene]]. Krauss learned by ear to play several songs from the album, including \"[[Tennessee Waltz]]\", which she practiced on violin with her mother accompanying on guitar. Krauss entered the talent contest in the novice category at the age of eight, placing fourth.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/64744236/decatur-the-birthplace-of-alison-krauss/ |title=Decatur the birthplace of Alison Krauss |date=September 18, 2017 |author=Staff |newspaper=[[Herald & Review]] |page=A3 |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref> (This is where she first met fiddler [[Andrea Zonn]], who won the junior division at age 10.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=sQ0EAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA37 |page=37 |title=Fiddler Zonn's 'Life' Puts Her in the Spotlight |date=May 17, 2003 |last=Bessman |first=Jim |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |volume=115 |number=20 |issn=0006-2510}}</ref>) Krauss investigated the bluegrass genre more thoroughly after this, and she developed a knack for learning complex [[riff]]s by ear, quickly turning them into her own version.<ref name=Argus1985/> In 1981\u201382, Krauss performed with Marvin Lee Flessner's country dance band, in which she fiddled and sang. In September 1983, her parents bought her a custom violin made by hand in Missouri&nbsp;\u2013 her first adult-sized instrument.<ref name=Graybill1984>{{cite news |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/64745341/alison-fiddle-better-than-anyone-else/ |title=Alison fiddles better than anyone else |date=November 24, 1984 |last=Graybill |first=Elaine |page=27 |newspaper=[[The Pantagraph]] |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref> At 13, she won the [[Walnut Valley Festival]] Fiddle Championship,<ref name=\"walnut\">{{cite web|title=1984 Walnut Valley Championship Archives&nbsp;\u2013 All Winners|publisher=[[Walnut Valley Festival]] official website|url=http://www.wvfest.com/contests/byyear.html?year=1984|access-date=February 7, 2007|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061110140655/http://www.wvfest.com/contests/byyear.html?year=1984|archive-date=November 10, 2006|df=mdy-all}}</ref> and the Society for the Preservation of Bluegrass in America named her the \"Most Promising Fiddler in the Midwest\".<ref>{{cite web|title=Alison Krauss interview|url=http://www.tvguide.com/celebrities/alison-krauss/bio/197694|website=TV Guide|access-date=July 2, 2012}}</ref> She was also called \"virtuoso\" by ''[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]'' magazine.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://newfavorite.proboards.com/thread/747/vanity-fair-names-alison-virtuoso |title=Vanity Fair names Alison 'Virtuoso' &#124; AKUS |website=Newfavorite.proboards.com |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref>\n\nKrauss first met [[Dan Tyminski]] around 1984 at a festival held by the Society. Every current member of her band, Union Station, first met her at these festivals.<ref name=\"gacvideo\">\"Interview with Alison Krauss and [[Dan Tyminski]]\" for ''The Collection'' on Great American Country, originally broadcast June 28, 2006; retrieved June 28, 2006.</ref>\n\n==Career==\n===1985\u20131991: Early career===\nKrauss made her recording debut in 1986 on the independent album, ''[[Different Strokes (Alison Krauss album)|Different Strokes]]'', in collaboration with Swamp Weiss and Jim Hoiles, and featuring her brother [[Viktor Krauss]]. From the age of 12 she performed with bassist and songwriter John Pennell in a band called \"Silver Rail\", replacing Andrea Zonn.<ref name=\"nytimes\">[https://www.nytimes.com/2000/04/30/nyregion/music-country-with-twang-and-pop.html MUSIC; \"Country, With Twang and Pop\"] by Robbie Wolvier for ''[[The New York Times]]''. April 30, 2000. Retrieved July 8, 2006.</ref> Pennell later changed the band's name to Union Station after another band was discovered with the name Silver Rail.<ref>[http://bluegrassmusic.com/content/2011/feature/alison-krauss-union-station/ \"Alison Krauss + Union Station Flight Plan: Paper Airplane Lands AKUS Back On The Bus\"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130801024005/http://bluegrassmusic.com/content/2011/feature/alison-krauss-union-station/ |date=August 1, 2013 }} by Larry Nager for Bluegrass Unlimited. Retrieved October 2, 2011.</ref>\n\nLater that year, she signed to Rounder Records, and in 1987, at 16, she released her debut album ''[[Too Late to Cry (Alison Krauss album)|Too Late to Cry]]'' with Union Station as her backup band.<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20070304011906/http://www.mtv.com/music/artist/krauss_alison/artist.jhtml#/music/artist/krauss_alison/bio.jhtml \"Alison Krauss \u2013 Full Biography\"] by Stephen Thomas Erlwine for Allmusic, hosted by MTV.com. Retrieved June 25, 2006.</ref>\n\nKrauss' debut solo album was quickly followed by her first group album with Union Station in 1989, ''[[Two Highways]]''.<ref name=\"cmtbio\">[https://web.archive.org/web/20040406185531/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/krauss_alison/bio.jhtml \"Alison Krauss Biography\"]. CMT.com. Retrieved June 6, 2006.</ref> The album includes the traditional tunes \"Wild Bill Jones\" and \"Beaumont Rag\", along with a bluegrass interpretation of [[The Allman Brothers Band|the Allman Brothers]]' \"[[Midnight Rider]]\".\n\nKrauss' contract with Rounder required her to alternate between releasing a solo album and an album with Union Station,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/64744769/krauss-standing-at-countrys-crossroads/ |title=Krauss standing at country's crossroads |date=February 27, 1990 |agency=[[Houston Chronicle]] |page=H3 |newspaper=[[The Dispatch / The Rock Island Argus|The Dispatch]] |via=[[Newspapers.com]]}}</ref> and she released the solo album ''[[I've Got That Old Feeling]]'' in 1990. It was her first album to rise onto the [[Billboard charts]], peaking in the top seventy-five on the [[Hot Country Songs|country chart]]. The album also was a notable point in her career as she earned her first [[Grammy Award]], the single \"Steel Rails\" was her first single tracked by Billboard, and the title single \"I've Got That Old Feeling\" was the first song for which she recorded a music video.\n\n===1992\u20131999: Rising success===\n{| Class=wikitable style=\"float:right;margin:0 0 0 1em;\"\n|-\n!colspan=2|Alison Krauss & Union Station\n|-\n!  style=\"text-align:center; vertical-align:bottom;\"|Name\n!  style=\"text-align:center; vertical-align:bottom;\"|Role\n|-\n|Alison Krauss\n|Lead vocals, piano, fiddle\n|-\n|Larry Atamanuik\n|Drums, percussion\n|-\n|[[Barry Bales]]\n|Bass\n|-\n|[[Ron Block]]\n|Guitar, [[banjo]]\n|-\n|[[Jerry Douglas (musician)|Jerry Douglas]]\n|[[Dobro]]\n|-\n|[[Dan Tyminski]]\n|Guitar, mandolin\n|}\nKrauss' second Union Station album ''[[Every Time You Say Goodbye]]'' was released in 1992, and she went on to win her second [[Grammy Award for Best Bluegrass Album]] of the year. She then joined the [[Grand Ole Opry]] in 1993 at the age of 21.<ref name=\"cmtbio\" /> She was the youngest cast member at the time, and the first bluegrass artist to join the Opry in 29 years.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.opry.com/artist/alison-krauss |title=ALISON KRAUSS &#124; Grand Ole Opry |website=Opry.com |date=July 3, 1993 |access-date=May 19, 2015 |archive-date=August 25, 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170825231306/https://www.opry.com/artist/alison-krauss |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web\n| title = Alison Krauss\n| url = http://www.opry.com/artists/k/Krauss_Alison.html\n| publisher = Grand Ole Opry\n| access-date = July 2, 2012\n| archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20121024143300/http://www.opry.com/artists/k/Krauss_Alison.html\n| archive-date = October 24, 2012\n| url-status = dead\n}}</ref><ref>{{cite web\n |title=Opry Member List PDF \n |url=http://www.opry.com/img/Opry%20Members%20List.pdf \n |date=April 23, 2012 \n |access-date=July 2, 2012 \n |url-status=dead \n |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120607030858/http://www.opry.com/img/Opry%20Members%20List.pdf \n |archive-date=June 7, 2012 \n}}</ref> She also collaborated on a project with [[the Cox Family]] in 1994, a bluegrass album called ''[[I Know Who Holds Tomorrow]]''. [[Mandolin]] and guitar player [[Dan Tyminski]] replaced Tim Stafford in Union Station in 1994. Late in the year, Krauss recorded with the band [[Shenandoah (band)|Shenandoah]] on its single \"[[Somewhere in the Vicinity of the Heart]]\", which brought her to the country music Top Ten for the first time and it won the [[Grammy Award for Best Country Collaboration with Vocals]]. Also in 1994, Krauss collaborated with [[Suzy Bogguss]], [[Kathy Mattea]], and [[Crosby, Stills, Nash & Young|Crosby, Stills, and Nash]] to contribute \"[[Teach Your Children]]\" to the AIDS benefit album [[Red Hot + Country]] produced by the [[Red Hot Organization]]. In 1997, she recorded vocals and violin for \"Half a Mind\", on [[Tommy Shaw]]'s [[7 Deadly Zens]] album.\n\n''[[Now That I've Found You: A Collection]]'', a compilation of older releases and some covers of her favorite works by other artists, was released in 1995. Some of these covers include [[Bad Company]]'s \"[[Desolation Angels (album)|Oh Atlanta]]\", [[the Foundations]]' & [[Daniel Joseph Schafer|Dan Schafer]]'s \"[[Baby, Now That I've Found You]]\", which was used in the Australian hit comedy movie [[The Castle (1997 Australian film)|''The Castle'']], and [[the Beatles]]' \"[[I Will]]\" with Tony Furtado.<ref>[http://www.rounder.com/?id=album.php&catalog_id=5930 \"Now That I've Found You\"] by Sidney Cox for Rounder Records. Retrieved June 12, 2006.</ref> A cover of [[Keith Whitley]]'s \"[[When You Say Nothing at All]]\" reached number three on the ''Billboard'' country chart;<ref>{{cite magazine |title=BillBoard Country Charts |url={{BillboardURLbyName|artist=alison krauss|chart=all}}|magazine=BillBoard\n|date=June 10, 1995|access-date=July 2, 2012}}</ref> the album peaked in the top fifteen on the all-genre [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] chart, and sold two million copies to become Krauss' first [[RIAA certification|double-platinum album]].<ref>{{cite web|title=BillBoard Chart History|url={{BillboardURLbyName|artist=alison krauss|chart=all}} |publisher=BillBoard |date=June 10, 1995 |access-date=July 2, 2012}}</ref> Krauss also was nominated for four [[Country Music Association Awards]] and won all of them.<ref>{{cite web|title=29th Annual CMA Awards|url=http://www.cmt.com/cma-awards/1995.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180210211241/http://www.cmt.com/cma-awards/1995.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=10 February 2018|website=CMT|access-date=3 October 2017}}</ref>\n\n''[[So Long So Wrong]]'', another Union Station album, was released in 1997 and won the [[Grammy Award for Best Bluegrass Album]]. One critic said its sound was \"rather untraditional\" and \"likely [to] change quite a few ... minds about bluegrass\".<ref>[http://georgegraham.com/krauss.html So Long, So Wrong] review by George Graham. \"The Graham Weekly Album Review No.&nbsp;1065\" as broadcast on WVIA-FM April 16, 1997. Retrieved June 12, 2006.</ref> Included on the album is the track \"It Doesn't Matter\", which was featured in the second-season premiere episode of ''[[Buffy the Vampire Slayer]]''<ref>\"[[When She Was Bad (Buffy episode)|When She Was Bad]]\", originally released September 15, 1997. Twentieth Century Fox and Joss Whedon.</ref> and was included on the ''Buffy'' soundtrack in 1999.\n\nHer next solo release in 1999, ''[[Forget About It]]'', included one of her two tracks to appear on the Billboard [[Adult Contemporary (chart)|adult contemporary chart]], \"Stay\". The album was certified gold and charted within the top seventy-five of the Billboard 200 and in the top five of the country chart. In addition, the track \"That Kind of Love\" was included in another episode of ''Buffy the Vampire Slayer.''<ref>\"[[Entropy (Buffy episode)|Entropy]]\", originally released April 30, 2002. Twentieth Century Fox and Joss Whedon.</ref>\n\n===2000\u2013present: Current career===\n[[Adam Steffey]] left Union Station in 1998, and was replaced by renowned [[dobro]] player [[Jerry Douglas]].<ref>[http://www.candaceasher.com/press.html \"September 2001: Review in \"Your Gazette\", Melbourne Australia by George Peden: 'These Ladies Are New Favourites.'\"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060615033249/http://candaceasher.com/press.html |date=June 15, 2006 }} by Candace Asher on CandaceAsher.com, September 2001. Retrieved June 6, 2006.</ref> Douglas had provided studio back-up to Krauss' records since 1987's ''Too Late to Cry''. Their next album, ''[[New Favorite]]'', was released on August 14, 2001. The album went on to win the Grammy for Best Bluegrass Album, with the single \"[[The Lucky One (Alison Krauss song)|The Lucky One]]\" winning a Grammy as well. ''New Favorite'' was followed up by the double platinum [[double album]] ''[[Live (Alison Krauss album)|Live]]'' in 2002 and a release of a DVD of the same live performance in 2003. Both the album and the DVD were recorded during a performance at [[The Louisville Palace]] and both the album and DVD have been certified double Platinum. Also in 2002 she played a singing voice for one of the characters in the animated comedy film ''[[Eight Crazy Nights]].''\n\n''[[Lonely Runs Both Ways]]'' was released in 2004, and eventually became another Alison Krauss & Union Station gold certified album. Ron Block described ''Lonely Runs Both Ways'' as \"pretty much... what we've always done\" in terms of song selection and the style, in which those songs were recorded.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/66004/krauss-runs-both-ways-on-new-album |title=Krauss 'Runs Both Ways' On New Album |website=Billboard.com |date=October 20, 2004 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref> Krauss believes the group \"was probably the most unprepared we've ever been\" for the album and that songs were chosen as needed rather than planned beforehand.<ref name=\"gac1\" /> She also performed a duet with [[Brad Paisley]] on his album ''[[Mud on the Tires]]'' in the single \"[[Whiskey Lullaby]]\". The single was quickly ranked in the top fifty of the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] and the top five of the [[Hot Country Songs]], and won the [[Country Music Association Awards]] for \"Best Musical Event\" and \"Best Music Video\" of the year.\n\n[[File:AlisonKraussCrossroads2007.jpg|thumb|Krauss in 2007]]\nIn 2007, Krauss and [[Robert Plant]] released the collaborative album titled ''[[Raising Sand]]''. RIAA-certified platinum, the album was nominated for and won five Grammy Awards<ref>{{cite web|author=mtv |url=http://www.mtv.com/news/1604582/robert-plant-and-alison-krauss-win-grammy-album-of-the-year/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140826140109/http://www.mtv.com/news/1604582/robert-plant-and-alison-krauss-win-grammy-album-of-the-year/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=August 26, 2014 |title=Robert Plant And Alison Krauss Win Grammy Album Of The Year |website=MTV.com |date=February 9, 2009 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.grammy.com/photos/alison-krauss-and-robert-plant-1 |title=Alison Krauss And Robert Plant |website=GRAMMY.com |date=February 8, 2009 |access-date=May 19, 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150521162418/http://www.grammy.com/photos/alison-krauss-and-robert-plant-1 |archive-date=May 21, 2015 |df=mdy-all }}</ref> at the [[51st Annual Grammy Awards]], including Album of the Year, Best Contemporary Folk/Americana Album, and Record of the Year (\"[[Please Read the Letter]]\"). Krauss and Plant recorded a Crossroads special in October 2007 for the [[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|Country Music Television]] network, which first aired on February 12, 2008.\n\nReturning with Union Station, Krauss released an album called ''[[Paper Airplane (album)|Paper Airplane]]'' on April 12, 2011,<ref>{{cite web|author=Elena See |url=https://www.npr.org/2011/04/14/134979466/first-listen-alison-krauss-and-union-station-paper-airplane |title=First Listen: Alison Krauss And Union Station, 'Paper Airplane' |publisher=NPR |date=April 3, 2011 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref> the follow-up album to ''Lonely Runs Both Ways'' (2004). [[Mike Shipley]], the recording and mixing engineer for the album, said that the album had a lengthy production time because of Krauss' non-stop migraines.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thenational.ae/arts-culture/music/alison-krauss-queen-of-bluegrass-music |title=Alison Krauss: Queen of Bluegrass music &#124; The National |website=Thenational.ae |date=November 23, 2011 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Klinge |first=Steve |url=http://articles.philly.com/2011-07-22/entertainment/29802192_1_barry-bales-alison-krauss-ron-block |title=Beautiful music despite the headaches - philly-archives |website=Articles.philly.com |date=July 22, 2011 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref> Nevertheless, ''Paper Airplane'' became Krauss's highest-charting album in the U.S., reaching number three on the ''Billboard'' 200 on topping both the country and bluegrass album charts.\n\nIn 2014, Krauss and her band Union Station toured with [[Willie Nelson and Family]], with special guests [[Kacey Musgraves]], and [[The Devil Makes Three (band)|the Devil Makes Three]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/music/2014/02/10/willie-nelson-and-alison-krauss-to-co-headline-tour/5358757/ |title=Spring, summer dates team Nelson and Family with Krauss and Union Station |website=USA Today |date=February 10, 2014 |access-date=June 29, 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/alison-krauss-willie-nelson-tour-dates/ |title=Willie Nelson and Alison Krauss Embarking on Co-Headlining Tour |website=Tasteofcountry.com |date=February 13, 2014 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref>\n\n[[Capitol Records]] released ''[[Windy City (Alison Krauss album)|Windy City]]'', an album of country and bluegrass classics, produced by [[Buddy Cannon]] and her first solo release in 17 years, on February 17, 2017.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Bernstein |first=Jonathan |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/country/videos/alison-krauss-on-nostalgic-new-solo-album-windy-city-w444779 |title=Alison Krauss on Nostalgic New Solo Album 'Windy City' |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=October 13, 2016 |access-date=February 23, 2017}}</ref> Krauss received two nominations at the [[60th Annual Grammy Awards]] for [[Best Country Solo Performance]] and [[Best American Roots Performance]].\n\nIn August 2021, Krauss announced she was releasing a sequel album to ''Raising Sand'' with Robert Plant called ''[[Raise the Roof (album)|Raise the Roof]]''.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Newman |first=Melinda |date=August 12, 2021 |title=Robert Plant & Alison Krauss Reunite for 'Raise the Roof' Album, 2022 Tour |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/9613758/robert-plant-alison-krauss-album-tour-raise-the-roof/ |access-date=August 12, 2021 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> The album was released in November that year, and Krauss and Plant went on tour as a duo in 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Rapp |first=Allison |date=2022-06-21 |title=Robert Plant and Alison Krauss Announce More US Tour Dates |url=https://ultimateclassicrock.com/robert-plant-alison-krauss-us-tour-2022/ |access-date=2024-01-15 |website=Ultimate Classic Rock |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Willman |first=Chris |date=2021-11-19 |title=Robert Plant and Alison Krauss Announce Summer 2022 Tour |url=https://variety.com/2021/music/news/robert-plant-alison-krauss-tour-summer-2022-1235115879/ |access-date=2024-01-15 |website=Variety |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n===Other work===\n[[File:KraussPlantNIA2008.JPG|thumb|250px|right|Krauss on stage with Robert Plant at Birmingham, England's [[National Indoor Arena|NIA]] on May 5, 2008]]\nKrauss has made guest appearances on other records on lead vocals, [[Vocal harmony|harmony vocals]], and [[fiddle]]. In 1987, at the age of 15, she played fiddle on the album ''The Western Illinois Rag'' by Americana musician Chris Vallillo. In 1993 she recorded vocals for the [[Phish]] song \"If I Could\" in Los Angeles.<ref>[http://www.phish.com/bandhistory/index.php?year=1993 \"Phish&nbsp;\u2013 Band History\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091123085309/http://www.phish.com/bandhistory/index.php?year=1993 |date=November 23, 2009 }}. Retrieved December 10, 2009.</ref> In 1997 she sang harmony vocals in both English and Irish on the album ''[[Runaway Sunday]]'' by [[Folk music of Ireland|Irish traditional]] band [[Altan (band)|Altan]]. In 1998 she played and sang on the title track of Hawaiian slack-key artist [[Ledward Kaapana]]'s album, ''Waltz of the Wind''.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/waltz-of-the-wind-mw0000600634 |title=Ledward Kaapana: Waltz of the Wind |author=<!--Not stated--> |date=n.d. |website=AllMusic |access-date=December 19, 2021}}</ref>\n\nKrauss had her only number one hit in 2000, receiving vocal credit for \"Buy Me a Rose\". She has contributed to numerous motion picture soundtracks, most notably ''[[O Brother, Where Art Thou? (soundtrack)|O Brother, Where Art Thou?]]'' (2000). She and [[Dan Tyminski]] contributed multiple tracks, including \"[[I'll Fly Away#Alison Krauss and Gillian Welch|I'll Fly Away]]\" (with [[Gillian Welch]]), \"Down to the River to Pray\", and \"I Am a Man of Constant Sorrow\". In the film, Tyminski's vocals on \"I Am a Man of Constant Sorrow\" were used for [[George Clooney]]'s character.<ref>[http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/entertainment/music/1845962.stm \"O Brother, Why Art Thou So Popular?\"]. BBC News, February 28, 2002. Retrieved June 25, 2006.</ref> The soundtrack sold over seven million copies and won the Grammy for Album of the Year in 2002.<ref>{{cite web|author=Evan Cater |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/o-brother-where-art-thou-mw0000106868 |title=O Brother, Where Art Thou? - Original Soundtrack &#124; Songs, Reviews, Credits, Awards |website=[[AllMusic]] |date=February 5, 2000 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref> Both Krauss and the surprisingly popular album were credited<ref name=\"npr\">[https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=1138127 \"Interview] on [[NPR]] ''Morning Edition''\". Bob Edwards, NPR, February 15, 2002. Retrieved July 10, 2006.</ref> with reviving interest in bluegrass. She has said, however, that she believes Americans already liked bluegrass and other less-heard musical genres, and that the film merely provided easy exposure to the music.<ref name=\"pbsinterview\">[https://web.archive.org/web/20021022111958/http://www.pbs.org/klru/austin/interviews/akrauss_interview.html \"Jerry Douglas and Ron Block of Union Station discuss their role in bluegrass music\"], PBS.org, May 3, 2002, via the Wayback Machine. Retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> She did not appear in the movie, at her own request, because she was pregnant during its filming.<ref name=\"b&n\">{{cite web|title=Country: O Sister! Bluegrass Star Alison Krauss's New Favorite: Hers and Ours|url=http://music.barnesandnoble.com/features/interview.asp?z=y&NID=452516|publisher=Barnes and Noble |date=August 14, 2001|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120214002753/http://music.barnesandnoble.com/features/interview.asp?z=y&NID=452516|archive-date=February 14, 2012}}</ref>\n\nIn 2007, Krauss released ''[[A Hundred Miles or More: A Collection]],'' an album of new songs, soundtrack tunes, and duets with artists such as [[John Waite]], [[James Taylor]], [[Brad Paisley]], and [[Natalie MacMaster]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://countrymusic.about.com/od/cdreviewsal/fr/100MilesOrMore.htm |title=Alison Krauss - A Hundred Miles Or More: A Collection |website=Countrymusic.about.com |date=July 21, 2012 |access-date=May 19, 2015 |archive-date=May 19, 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150519231054/http://countrymusic.about.com/od/cdreviewsal/fr/100MilesOrMore.htm |url-status=dead }}</ref> The album was  successful commercially but given a lukewarm reception by critics.<ref>{{cite web|author=James Christopher Monger |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/a-hundred-miles-or-more-a-collection-mw0000746674 |title=A Hundred Miles or More: A Collection - Alison Krauss &#124; Songs, Reviews, Credits, Awards |website=[[AllMusic]] |date=April 3, 2007 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref> One of the tracks, \"[[Missing You (John Waite song)|Missing You]]\", a duet with Waite (and a cover of his hit single from 1984), was similarly received as a single. On August 11, television network [[Great American Country]] aired a one-hour special, ''Alison Krauss: A Hundred Miles or More'', based on the album.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.gactv.com/gac/shows_spl/episode/0,,gac_26200_51876,00.html |title=On TV : Special : Alison Krauss: A Hundred Miles or More : Great American Country |publisher=GACTCV |date=April 15, 2015 |access-date=May 19, 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://archive.today/20140824085144/http://www.gactv.com/gac/shows_spl/episode/0,,gac_26200_51876,00.html |archive-date=August 24, 2014 |df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\nKrauss appeared on [[Heart (band)|Heart]]'s March 2010 concert DVD ''Night at Sky Church'', providing the lead vocals for the song \"[[These Dreams]]\".<ref>[http://www.seattlepi.com/ae/music/article/Music-DVD-Review-Heart-Night-at-Sky-Church-1079088.php \"Music Review \u2013 Night At Sky Church\"]. Jack Goodstein, April 26, 2011, SeattlePI.com.</ref>\n\nOther soundtracks for which Krauss has performed include ''[[Twister (1996 film)#Soundtracks|Twister]]'', ''[[The Prince of Egypt (soundtrack)|The Prince of Egypt]]'', ''[[Eight Crazy Nights#Soundtrack|Eight Crazy Nights]]'', ''[[Mona Lisa Smile#Soundtrack|Mona Lisa Smile]]'', ''[[Divine Secrets of the Ya-Ya Sisterhood (film)|Divine Secrets of the Ya-Ya Sisterhood]]'', ''[[Alias (TV series)|Alias]]'', ''[[Bambi II#Soundtrack|Bambi II]]'' and ''[[Cold Mountain (soundtrack)|Cold Mountain]]''. She contributed \"Jubilee\" to the 2004 documentary ''[[Paper Clips (film)|Paper Clips]]''. The ''Cold Mountain'' songs she sang, \"[[The Scarlet Tide]]\" with [[T Bone Burnett]] and [[Elvis Costello]], and \"[[You Will Be My Ain True Love]]\" with [[Sting (musician)|Sting]], were each nominated for an [[Academy Awards|Academy Award]]. She performed both songs at the [[76th Academy Awards]], the first with Costello and Burnett, and the other with Sting.<ref name=\"oscars\">[https://web.archive.org/web/20040215024955/http://www.oscars.org/press/pressreleases/2004/04.02.13.b.html \"Sting, Alison Krauss, Elvis Costello and T Bone Burnett to Perform at The 76th Academy Awards\"]. Press release by Toni Thompson for the [[Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences]] via the Wayback Machine on February 14, 2004. Retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> She produced [[Nickel Creek]]'s [[Nickel Creek (album)|debut album]] (2000) and the follow-up ''[[This Side]]'' (2002), which won Krauss her first Grammy award as a producer.\n\nKrauss performed on ''[[Moody Bluegrass (musical project)|Moody Bluegrass: A Nashville Tribute to the Moody Blues]]''.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=4247134 |title=Moody Bluegrass: Rocking Through the Hills |publisher=NPR |date=December 30, 2004 |access-date=August 25, 2015}}</ref>\n\nShe participated in [[William Edward Childs|Billy Childs']] 2014 tribute album to [[Laura Nyro]], ''Map to the Treasure: Reimagining Laura Nyro'', performing on the track \"[[And When I Die]]\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://blogs.wsj.com/speakeasy/2014/07/15/alison-krauss-joins-billy-childs-on-laura-nyros-and-when-i-die-exclusive/ |title=Alison Krauss Joins Billy Childs on Laura Nyro's 'And When I Die' (Exclusive) - Speakeasy |website=The Wall Street Journal |date=July 15, 2014 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/2014/09/06/346299259/stars-line-up-to-reimagine-laura-nyro |author=Simon, Scott |title=Stars Line Up To Reimagine Laura Nyro |publisher=NPR |date=September 6, 2014 |access-date=September 5, 2015}}</ref>\n\nKrauss also appears on [[Def Leppard]]'s twelfth studio album, ''[[Diamond Star Halos]]'', released March 2022, as a featured vocalist on the songs \"This Guitar\" and \"Lifeless\".<ref name=\"Erlewine\">{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/diamond-star-halos-mw0003687046 |title=Diamond Star Halos Review |last= Erlewine |first=Stephen Thomas |date=2022 |website=[[AllMusic]] |access-date=July 30, 2022}}</ref> Krauss duetted with [[High Valley]] on the group's 2023 single \"[[Do This Life]]\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.1009thecat.com/2023/01/16/high-valley-alison-krauss-do-this-life/|title=High Valley & Allison Kraus - Do This Life|work=100.9 The Cat|date=January 16, 2023|access-date=January 22, 2023}}</ref>\n\n==Reception and influences==\n[[File:Alison Krauss TFF.JPG|thumb|Krauss performing live in 2012]]\nKrauss' earliest musical experience was as an instrumentalist, though her style has grown to focus more on her vocals<ref name=\"cmtbio\" /> with a band providing most of the instrumentation. Musicians she enjoys include vocalists [[Lou Gramm]] of [[Foreigner (band)|Foreigner]] and [[Paul Rodgers]] of [[Bad Company]].<ref>[http://cgi.cnn.com/SHOWBIZ/Music/9911/16/wb.krauss/index.html Krauss cultivates bluegrass into crossover success] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060827092140/http://cgi.cnn.com/SHOWBIZ/Music/9911/16/wb.krauss/index.html |date=August 27, 2006 }} by Neil Curry for CNN on November 16, 1999. Retrieved June 29, 2006.</ref><ref>{{usurped|1=[https://archive.today/20120709073203/http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Artists/K/Krauss_Alison/1997/10/10/746703.html \"Alison Krauss 'comes out' on heavy metal\"]}} for JAM! Music by Jane Stevenson. Retrieved June 27, 2006.</ref><ref>[http://lubbockonline.com/news/101497/UX0381.htm \"Krauss still hanging on to eclectic style\"] for the ''Los Angeles Times''/''The Washington Post'' on October 13, 1997. Retrieved June 29, 2006.</ref> Krauss' family listened to \"folk records\" while she was growing up, but she had friends who exposed her to such acts as [[AC/DC]], [[Carly Simon]], [[the Rolling Stones]], [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]], and [[Electric Light Orchestra|ELO]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Alison Krauss interview for the release of Essential Alison Krauss |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/rockandpopfeatures/5887939/Alison-Krauss-interview-for-the-release-of-Essential-Alison-Krauss.html |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220111/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/rockandpopfeatures/5887939/Alison-Krauss-interview-for-the-release-of-Essential-Alison-Krauss.html |archive-date=January 11, 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |work=The Daily Telegraph |first=Paul |last=Sexton |date=July 22, 2009 |access-date=July 29, 2009 |location=London }}{{cbignore}}</ref> She cites [[Dolly Parton]], with whom she has since collaborated a number of times, as a major influence. Some credit Krauss and Union Station, at least partially, with a recent revival of interest in bluegrass music in the United States.<ref name=\"npr\" /> Despite being together for nearly two decades and winning numerous awards, she said the group was \"just beginning right now\" (in 2002) because \"in spite of all the great things that have happened for the band, [she] feel[s] musically it's just really beginning\".<ref name=\"pbsinterview\" /> Although she alternates between solo releases and works with the band, she has said there is no difference in her involvement between the two.<ref name=\"b&n\" />\n\nAs a group, AKUS have been called \"American favourites\", \"world-beaters\",<ref>[https://www.bbc.co.uk/music/reviews/hpqv \"Alison Krauss & Union Station Live Review\"] by Chris Jones for BBC. Retrieved June 15, 2006.</ref> and \"the tightest band around\".<ref name=\"bbclonely\">[https://www.bbc.co.uk/music/folkcountry/reviews/alisonkrauss_lonely.shtml \"Alison Krauss & Union Station Lonely Runs Both Ways Review\"] by Sue Keogh for BBC. Retrieved June 15, 2006.</ref> While they have been successful as a group, many reviews note Krauss still \"remains the undisputed star and rock-solid foundation\" and have described her as the \"band's focus\"<ref name=\"bgwlonely\">[http://www.bluegrassworks.com/review.php?reviewID=112 \"Alison Krauss & Union Station \u2013 Lonely Runs Both Ways (CD, 2004)\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061005195451/http://www.bluegrassworks.com/review.php?reviewID=112 |date=October 5, 2006 }} by Ben Fitzgerald, Bluegrass Works, December 13, 2006. Retrieved June 15, 2006.</ref> with an \"angelic\"<ref name=\"bbclonely\" /> voice that \"flows like honey\".<ref name=\"bgwlonely\" /> Her work has been compared to that of [[the Cox Family]], [[Bill Monroe]], and [[Del McCoury]],{{Citation needed|date=April 2010}} and has in turn been credited with influencing various \"[[progressive bluegrass|Newgrass]]\" artists including Nickel Creek, for which she acted as record producer on two of their albums.<ref name=\"kraussabout\">[http://folkmusic.about.com/od/artistsaz/p/AlisonKrauss.htm \"Alison Krauss and Union Station\"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060615030852/http://folkmusic.about.com/od/artistsaz/p/AlisonKrauss.htm |date=June 15, 2006}} by Kim Ruehl on FolkMusic.About.com. Retrieved June 24, 2006.</ref> In addition to her work with Nickel Creek, she has acted as producer to the Cox Family, [[Reba McEntire]] and [[Alan Jackson]].<ref>[https://archive.today/20120904200845/http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_headlines/article/0,,GAC_26063_4724117,00.html \"Alison Krauss Produces Alan Jackson\"] from Great American Country on May 10, 2006 citing ''The Tennessean''. Retrieved June 26, 2006.</ref> [[Adam Sweeting]] of ''[[The Guardian]]'' has said Krauss and Union Station are \"superb, when they stick to [[hoedown]]s and [[old-time music|hillbilly music]], but much less convincing, when they lurch towards the middle of the road\".<ref>[http://arts.guardian.co.uk/reviews/story/0,11712,1354230,00.html \"Alison Krauss and Union Station, Lonely Runs Both Ways (Rounder Records)\"] by [[Adam Sweeting]] for The Guardian (UK). November 19, 2004. Retrieved June 15, 2006.</ref> ''[[Blender (magazine)|Blender magazine]]'' has said the \"flavorless repertoire [Krauss] sings... steers her toward Lite FM\".<ref>[http://www.metacritic.com/music/artists/kraussalison/lonelyrunsbothways \"Lonely Runs Both Ways\"] on Metacritic originally from ''Blender magazine'' Jan/Feb 2005. Retrieved June 15, 2006.</ref> In addition, [[Q magazine|''Q'' magazine]] and [[The Onion|''The Onion'' AV Club]] have said their newer releases are \"pretty much the usual\", and that although Krauss is generally \"adventurous\", these recent releases contain nothing to \"alienate the masses\".<ref>[http://www.metacritic.com/music/artists/kraussalison/newfavorite \"New Favorite\"] on Metacritic, originally from ''Q Magazine'' September 2001 and ''The Onion'' AV Club. Retrieved June 15, 2006.</ref>\n\n===Voice, themes, and musical style===\nKrauss possesses a [[soprano]] voice, which has been described as \"angelic\".<ref name=\"bbclonely\" /><ref>{{cite magazine |first=Will |last=Hermes |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/albumreviews/paper-airplane-20110411 |title=Alison Krauss and Union Station \u2013 Review |magazine=Rolling Stone |date=April 11, 2011 |access-date=January 20, 2012}}</ref> \n[[File:Alison Krauss 2011.jpg|thumb|Krauss at the 2011 IBMAs]]\nShe has said her musical influences include [[J. D. Crowe]], [[Ricky Skaggs]], and [[Tony Rice]].<ref>[http://www.dirtynelson.com/linen/102/krauss.html New Favorite] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060212012807/http://www.dirtynelson.com/linen/102/krauss.html |date=February 12, 2006 }} by Kerry Dexter from Dirty Linen No.&nbsp;102 Oct/Nov 2. Retrieved June 29, 2006.</ref> Many of her songs are described as sad,<ref>{{usurped|1=[https://archive.today/20120709161646/http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Artists/K/Krauss_Alison/1999/08/18/746702.html \"Sad songs, migraines don't get Alison Krauss down\"]}} by David Veitch for JAM! Music. Retrieved June 27, 2006.</ref> and are often about [[romantic love|love]], especially lost love. Though Krauss has a close involvement with her group and a long career in music, she rarely performs music she has written herself. She has also described her general approach to constructing an album as starting with a single song and selecting other tracks based on the first, to give the final album a somewhat consistent theme and mood.<ref name=\"b&n\" /><ref name=\"revive\">{{cite news|last=Dickie|first=Mary|title=Alison Krauss tends bluegrass revival|url=http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Artists/K/Krauss_Alison/2005/05/11/1034228.html |work=JAM! Music |date=May 11, 2005 |access-date=August 30, 2024 |url-status=dead|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130115065444/http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Artists/K/Krauss_Alison/2005/05/11/1034228.html|archive-date=January 15, 2013}}</ref> She most commonly performs in the bluegrass and country genres, though she has had two songs on the [[adult contemporary music|adult contemporary]] charts, has worked with rock artists such as [[Phish]]<ref name=\"cmtbio\" /> and [[Sting (musician)|Sting]],<ref name=\"oscars\" /> and is sometimes said to stray into pop music.<ref name=\"nytimes\" /><ref>[http://georgegraham.com/reviews/akus4.html \"Alison Krauss & Union Station: New Favorite\"] by George Graham, The Graham Weekly Album Review No.&nbsp;1250 broadcast on WVIA-FM August 18, 2001. Retrieved July 8, 2006.</ref>\n\n===Music videos===\nKrauss did not think she would make music videos at the beginning of her career. After recording her first she was convinced it was so bad that she would never do another. Nonetheless, she has continued to make further videos. Many of the first videos she saw were by bluegrass artists. [[Dan Tyminski]] has noted that the [[Michael Jackson's Thriller (music video)|video for ''Thriller'']] was very popular at the time she was first exposed to music videos. She has made suggestions on the style or theme to some videos, though she tends to leave such decisions to the [[music video director|director]] of the particular video. The group chooses directors by seeking out people who have previously directed videos that band members have enjoyed. The director for a video to \"If I Didn't Know Any Better\" from ''Lonely Runs Both Ways'', for example, was selected because Krauss enjoyed work he had done with [[Def Leppard]] and, she wondered, what he could do with their music. While style decisions are generally left to the various directors of the videos, many&nbsp;\u2013 including for \"[[The Lucky One (Alison Krauss song)|The Lucky One]]\", \"Restless\", \"Goodbye is All We Have\", \"New Favorite\", and \"If I Didn't Know Any Better\" \u2013 follow a pattern. In all of these videos Krauss walks, sometimes interacting with other people, while the rest of the band follows her.<ref name=\"gacvideo\" /><ref name=\"gacinterview\">[http://www.gactv.com/gac/shows_ngt/episode/0,,GAC_26155_44020,00.html Interview with Alison Krauss and Dan Tyminski] on ''GAC Nights''{{dead link|date=July 2017 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}. [[Great American Country]] originally broadcast June 27, 2006; retrieved June 28, 2006.</ref>\n\n===Performances===\nKrauss has said she used to dislike working in the studio, where she had to perform the same song repeatedly, but has come to like studio work roughly the same as [[concert|live stage performances]]. Her own favorite concert experiences include watching three [[Foreigner (band)|Foreigner]] concerts during a single tour, a [[Dolly Parton]] concert, and a [[Larry Sparks]] concert.<ref>Interview with Krauss from the ''Alison Krauss + Union Station: Live'' DVD by Rounder Records released in 2003.</ref>\n\nShe appeared on ''[[Austin City Limits]]'' in 1992 and opened the show in 1995 with Union Station.<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20011111154844/http://www.pbs.org/klru/austin/artists/program85.html \"Alison Krauss on Austin City Limits\"] from PBS from 1996 via the Wayback Machine; retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> The ''New Favorite'' tour, after AKUS' album of the same name, was planned to start September 12, 2001 in [[Cincinnati, Ohio]], but was delayed until September 28 in [[Savannah, Georgia]] following the [[September 11, 2001 attacks|September 11 terrorist attacks]].<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20021017222631/http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1448899/09172001/krauss_alison.jhtml COUNTRY BEAT: Alison Krauss, Wynonna Judd, Dolly Parton ...] for MTV.com on September 17, 2001; retrieved June 25, 2006.</ref> Krauss took part in the ''Down from the Mountain'' tour in 2002, which featured many artists from the ''[[O Brother, Where Art Thou? (soundtrack)|O Brother, Where Art Thou]]'' soundtrack.<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20030223071632/http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1450115/10172001/krauss_alison.jhtml \"Krauss, Loveless Among Down From The Mountain Headliners\"] for MTV.com on October 17, 2001; retrieved June 25, 2006.</ref><ref>[http://www.jimdirden.com/concert_reviews/dftm.htm \"Down from the Mountain tour\"] by Jim Durden for Tomlin Communications on July 20, 2002; retrieved June 25, 2006.</ref> ''Down from the Mountain'' was followed by the ''Great High Mountain Tour'', which was composed of musicians from both ''O Brother'' and ''Cold Mountain'', including Krauss.<ref name=\"gacinterview\" /> She has also given several notable smaller performances including at [[Carnegie Hall]] (with the [[Grand Ole Opry]]),<ref>[https://archive.today/20130123142622/http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_headlines/article/0,,GAC_26063_4729294,00.html \"Carnegie Hall performance\"] at Great American Country March 1, 2006; retrieved June 26, 2006.</ref> on [[Lifetime Television]] in a concert of female performers, on the radio show ''[[A Prairie Home Companion]]'',<ref>[http://prairiehome.publicradio.org/programs/2004/05/01/index.shtml \"Program details\"] from Prairie Home Companion on May 1, 2006; retrieved June 26, 2006.</ref> where she sang two songs not previously recorded on any of her albums, and a performance at the [[White House]] attended by then-President [[Bill Clinton]] and then-Vice President [[Al Gore]].<ref>[http://www.cybergrass.com/Articles/ak-white.html \"Alison Krauss at the White House\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070514011111/http://www.cybergrass.com/Articles/ak-white.html |date=May 14, 2007 }} by Marian Leighton Levy at Rounder Records May 18, 1995; retrieved June 29, 2006.</ref> She has also been in the [[White House]] again, performing the song \"[[When You Say Nothing at All]]\"<ref>{{cite web |url=https://obamawhitehouse.archives.gov/photos-and-video/video/2011/11/21/alison-krauss-performs-when-you-say-nothing-all-country-music-perf |title=Alison Krauss performs \"When You Say Nothing at All\" at Country Music: In Performance at the White House &#124; The White House |date=November 21, 2011 |via=[[NARA|National Archives]] |work=[[whitehouse.gov]] |df=mdy-all |access-date=May 19, 2015 }}</ref> at country music performances. She also performed a tribute to [[the Everly Brothers]] at which she sang \"[[All I Have to Do is Dream]]\" with [[Emmylou Harris]] and \"[[When Will I Be Loved (song)|When Will I Be Loved]]\" with [[Vince Gill]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/vince-gill-emmylou-harris-alison-krauss-music-masters/ |title=Vince Gill, Alison Krauss Pay Tribute to the Everly Brothers |website=Theboot.com |date=October 27, 2014 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.rttnews.com/2403853/vince-gill-alison-krauss-and-emmylou-harris-pay-tribute-to-everly-brothers.aspx |title=Vince Gill, Alison Krauss And Emmylou Harris Pay Tribute To Everly Brothers |website=Rttnews.com |date=October 27, 2014 |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref> She was also invited by [[Taylor Swift]] to perform with her at the 2013 CMA's and by [[Joshua Bell]] to perform with him on a Christmas album; Bell said that \"she (Krauss) is someone I've adored for so many years now\".<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.joshuabell.com/news/musical-gifts-joshua-bell-friends-available-now-pre-order |title=Musical Gifts From Joshua Bell & Friends Available Now for Pre-Order &#124; The Official Joshua Bell Site |website=Joshuabell.com |access-date=May 19, 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151019090122/http://www.joshuabell.com/news/musical-gifts-joshua-bell-friends-available-now-pre-order |archive-date=October 19, 2015 |df=mdy-all }}</ref> She performed at DAR Constitution Hall in Washington, D.C., on January 10, 2015, as a part of \"The Life and Songs of Emmylou Harris: An All Star Concert Celebration\" which is a tribute to [[Emmylou Harris]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/6327421/alison-krauss-emmylou-harris-tribute-concert |title=Alison Krauss Joins Emmylou Harris Tribute Concert |website=Billboard.com |access-date=May 19, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://radio.com/2014/11/21/alison-krauss-conor-oberst-emmylou-harris-tribute-concert/ |title=Alison Krauss, Conor Oberst Added to Emmylou Harris Tribute Concert \u00ab |website=Radio.com |date=November 21, 2014 |access-date=May 19, 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141207193017/http://radio.com/2014/11/21/alison-krauss-conor-oberst-emmylou-harris-tribute-concert/ |archive-date=December 7, 2014 |url-status=dead |df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\n==Awards and honors==\n{{Main|List of awards and nominations received by Alison Krauss}}\n[[File:Alison Krauss at Rockygrass 2005.jpg|thumb|Krauss with her band Union Station]]\nKrauss has won twenty-seven [[Grammy Award]]s<ref>[[List of awards and nominations received by Alison Krauss]]. List of Alison Krauss' awards. Retrieved February 13, 2012.</ref> over the course of her career as a solo artist, as a group with Union Station, as a duet with [[Robert Plant]], and as a record producer. As of 2021, she ranks fourth on the list of winners of the [[Grammy Award records|most Grammy Awards]].<ref>[http://www.properdistribution.com/news/full-story.php?pg=6&id=45 \"Alison Krauss & Union Station Win Three Trophies at Grammy's\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070516013150/http://www.properdistribution.com/news/full-story.php?pg=6&id=45 |date=May 16, 2007 }} for Proper Music Distribution on February 20, 2006; retrieved June 5, 2006.</ref> She overtook [[Aretha Franklin]] for the most female wins at the [[Grammy Awards of 2004|46th Grammy Awards]], where Krauss won three, bringing her total at the time to seventeen (Franklin won her sixteenth that night).<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20040227214603/http://www.shorefire.com/artists/akrauss/pr_akrauss_02_09_04.html \"Rounder recording artist becomes Grammy's most-honored female musician\"], Press release on Shorefire and the Los Angeles Times by Jen Chapin and Robert Hilburn on February 9, 2004 via the Wayback Machine. Last accessed July 28, 2009.</ref> The [[National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences|Recording Academy]] (which presents the Grammy Awards) presented her with a special musical achievement honor in 2005.<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20060901053608/http://www.cmt.com/artists/news/1513293/11082005/krauss_alison.jhtml \"Recording Academy Honors Krauss, Scruggs, McGraw and the Winans\"] by Edward Morris for CMT.com on November 8, 2005; retrieved June 7, 2006.</ref> She has also won 14 [[International Bluegrass Music Association|International Bluegrass Music Association Awards]],<ref name=\"IMBAAwins\">[http://www.ibma.org/ibma.awards/recipients/index.asp \"Past International Bluegrass Music Association Awards Recipients\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090223141121/http://www.ibma.org/ibma.awards/recipients/index.asp |date=February 23, 2009 }} for IMBA.org. Retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> 9 [[Country Music Association Awards]],<ref name=\"CMAAwins1\">[http://www.cmaawards.com/2008/database/ArtistDetail.aspx?artistId=40 Alison Krauss's CMA Awards] from CMAAwards.com. Retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref><ref name=\"CMAAwins2\">[http://www.cmaawards.com/2008/database/ArtistDetail.aspx?artistId=1039 \"Alison Krauss and Union Station's CMA Awards\"] from CMAAwards.com; retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> 2 [[GMA Dove Award|Gospel Music Association Awards]], 2 [[CMT Music Awards]],<ref name=\"CMTA05\">[https://web.archive.org/web/20090602204653/http://www.cmt.com/microsites/cmt-music-awards/archives/2005.jhtml \"2005 Awards archive\"] from CMT.com; retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref><ref name=\"CMTA08\">[https://web.archive.org/web/20090523104809/http://www.cmt.com/microsites/cmt-music-awards/archives/2008.jhtml 2008 Awards archive] from CMT.com; retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref><ref name=\"CMTA09\">[https://web.archive.org/web/20080208113542/http://www.cmt.com/cmt-music-awards/nominees.jhtml 2009 Awards archive] from CMT.com; retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> 2 [[Academy of Country Music|Academy of Country Music Awards]],<ref name=\"ACMwin\">[http://www.acmcountry.com/awards/awardsSearch.php?queryStr=krauss \"Alison Krauss ACM wins and nominations\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110610170110/http://www.acmcountry.com/awards/awardsSearch.php?queryStr=krauss |date=June 10, 2011 }} by acmcountry.com. Retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> and 1 [[Canadian Country Music Association|Canadian Country Music Award]].<ref name=\"CCMAwin\">[http://ccma.org/awards/awards_archives.cfm?SelectedAwardYear=2000 \"2000 CCMA Award winners\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100612223733/http://ccma.org/awards/awards_archives.cfm?SelectedAwardYear=2000 |date=June 12, 2010 }} on CCMA.org. Retrieved July 28, 2009.</ref> [[Country Music Television]] ranked Krauss 12th on their \"40 Greatest Women of Country Music\" list in 2002.<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20040313060707/http://www.cmt.com/shows/dyn/greatest_series/76608/episode_countdown.jhtml \"CMT's 40 Greatest Women of Country Music\"] on CMT.com; retrieved July 27, 2009.</ref>\n\nAt the [[76th Academy Awards]] in February 2004, where she performed two nominated songs from the ''[[Cold Mountain (film)|Cold Mountain]]'' soundtrack, Krauss was chosen by Hollywood shoe designer [[Stuart Weitzman]] to wear a pair of $2 million 'Cinderella' sandals with 4\u00bd inch clear glass stiletto heels and two straps adorned with 565 Kwiat diamonds set in platinum. Feeling like a rather unglamorous choice, Krauss said, \"When I first heard, I was like, 'What were they thinking?' I have the worst feet of anybody who will be there that night!\" In addition to the fairy-tale-inspired shoes, Weitzman outfitted Krauss with a [[Palm Tr\u0113o]] 600 smartphone, bejeweled with 3,000 clear-and-topaz-colored [[Swarovski]] crystals. The shoes were returned, but Krauss kept the crystal-covered phone. Weitzman chose Krauss to show off his fashions at the urging of his daughters, who are fans of Krauss' music.<ref>Lee, Lisa. [https://web.archive.org/web/20070706191937/http://www.cmt.com/artists/news/1485404/20040227/krauss_alison.jhtml \"'Cinderella' Krauss Tries On Her Slippers\".] [[Country Music Television|CMT.com.]], February 27, 2004; retrieved October 31, 2007.</ref><ref>[http://www.geekzone.co.nz/content.asp?ContentId=2381 \"Grammy Award-winner Alison Krauss to carry Swarovski crystal-clad Treo 600 smartphone\"] by Geekzone.co.nz; retrieved November 1, 2007.</ref>\n\n[[File:AlisonKraussWay.jpg|thumb|Honorary Alison Krauss Way in Champaign, Illinois]]\nIn May 2012, Alison Krauss was awarded an Honorary Doctorate of Music from [[Berklee College of Music]].<ref>{{cite web |last=Betts |first=Stephen L. |url=http://theboot.com/alison-krauss-eagles-berklee-college-of-music-honor/ |title=Alison Krauss, Eagles to Receive Berklee College of Music Honorary Degrees |website=Theboot.com |date=April 3, 2012 |access-date=February 23, 2017}}</ref>\n\nIn March 2015, her hometown of Champaign, Illinois, designated the 400 block of West Hill Street as \"Honorary Alison Krauss Way\".<ref name=\"Pressey\">{{cite news |last=Pressey |first=Debra |date=March 7, 2015 |title=Krauss might get her way |url=http://www.news-gazette.com/news/local/2015-03-07/krauss-might-get-her-way.html |work=The News-Gazette |location=Champaign, IL |access-date=March 16, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Crane |first=Tracy |date=March 26, 2017 |title=What's in a name? |url=http://www.news-gazette.com/news/local/2017-03-26/whats-name.html |work=The News-Gazette |location=Champaign, IL |access-date=March 16, 2019}}</ref>\n\nOn April 13, 2024, Krauss became a recipient of the [[The Lincoln Academy of Illinois#Order of Lincoln Award|Order of Lincoln]], which is Illinois' highest civilian honor.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.illinois.gov/news/press-release.29628.html |title=Gov. Pritzker Announces the 2024 Order of Lincoln Recipients |date=February 12, 2024 |access-date=April 13, 2024}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nKrauss was married to musician [[Pat Bergeson]] from 1997 to 2001.<ref>{{cite book |title=Musicians and Composers of the 20th Century |volume=3 |page=798 |last=Cramer |first=Alfred W. |publisher=Salem Press |year=2009 |isbn=978-1587655159}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Menaker |first=Daniel |title=AT HOME WITH/Alison Krauss; O Superstar, Where Art Thou?   |work=[[The New York Times]]|date=January 24, 2002 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2002/01/24/garden/at-home-with-alison-krauss-o-superstar-where-art-thou.html  }}</ref> They have one child, born in 1999.<ref>{{cite book |title=Biography Today: Profiles of People of Interest to Young Readers |url=https://archive.org/details/biographytodaypr0000abbe_a6z3 |url-access=registration |page=[https://archive.org/details/biographytodaypr0000abbe_a6z3/page/271 271] |first1=Cherie D. |last1=Abbey |author2=Omnigraphics |first3=Kevin |last3=Hillstrom |publisher=Omnigraphics |year=2005 |isbn=0780806921}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|Alison Krauss discography}}\n;Studio albums\n*1986: ''[[Different Strokes (Alison Krauss album)|Different Strokes]]'' <small>(with Jim Hoiles and Swamp Weiss)</small>\n*1987: ''[[Too Late to Cry (Alison Krauss album)|Too Late to Cry]]''\n*1989: ''[[Two Highways (album)|Two Highways]]'' <small>(with [[Union Station (band)|Union Station]])</small>\n*1990: ''[[I've Got That Old Feeling]]''\n*1992: ''[[Every Time You Say Goodbye]]'' <small>(with Union Station)</small>\n*1994: ''[[I Know Who Holds Tomorrow]]'' <small>(with [[the Cox Family]])</small>\n*1997: ''[[So Long So Wrong]]'' <small>(with Union Station)</small> \n*1999: ''[[Forget About It]]'' \n*2001: ''[[New Favorite]]'' <small>(with Union Station)</small>\n*2004: ''[[Lonely Runs Both Ways]]'' <small>(with Union Station)</small> \n*2007: ''[[Raising Sand]]'' <small>(with [[Robert Plant]])</small>\n*2011: ''[[Paper Airplane (album)|Paper Airplane]]'' <small>(with Union Station)</small>\n*2017: ''[[Windy City (Alison Krauss album)|Windy City]]''\n*2021: ''[[Raise the Roof (album)|Raise the Roof]]'' <small>(with [[Robert Plant]])</small>\n\n==Filmography==\n{| class=\"wikitable sortable\"\n|+ List of film credits\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Alecia_Nugent","to":"Alecia Nugent"}],"pages":{"24206152":{"pageid":24206152,"ns":0,"title":"Alecia Nugent","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2014}}\n\n{{BLP primary sources|date=September 2009}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name         = Alecia Nugent\n| image        =\n| birth_place  =\n| birth_date   = 1972\n| origin       = Hickory Grove, [[Louisiana]], US\n| genre        = [[Bluegrass music|Bluegrass]]\n| occupation   = Singer, musician\n| years_active = 1996\u2013present\n| label        = [[Rounder Records|Rounder]]\n| website      = http://www.alecianugent.com\n}}\n\n'''Alecia Nugent''' (born in Hickory Grove, Louisiana) is a [[parish music|country]], [[Americana (music)|Americana]], [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]] vocalist and musician.  Alecia has worked with bluegrass legend [[Carl Jackson]] on all of her albums.  Alecia was nominated for IBMA Female Vocalist of The Year in 2009.<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.alecianugent.com/news.htm |title=Alecia Nugent&#124;Hillbilly Goddess, Rounder, Americana, Bluegrass,Country, Roots Music |access-date=September 4, 2009 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100106135916/http://www.alecianugent.com/news.htm |archive-date=January 6, 2010 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.rounder.com/ibma/2009/nominations.html |title=Rounder Records 2009 IBMA Awards Nominations |website=www.rounder.com |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090915182159/http://www.rounder.com/ibma/2009/nominations.html |archive-date=2009-09-15}}</ref>\n\n==Touring==\nNugent performed in Scarborough, Ontario, Canada in 2008 as part of the Bluegrass Sundays Winter Concert Series.<ref>''Strings'', newsletter of the Pineridge Bluegrass Folklore Society, December 2007</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! style=\"width:16em;\"| Title\n! style=\"width:18em;\"| Details\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Alecia Nugent''\n| \n* Release date: March 9, 2004\n* Label: [[Rounder Records]]\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''A Little Girl\u2026A Big Four-Lane''\n| \n* Release date: February 28, 2006\n* Label: Rounder Records\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Hillbilly Goddess''\n| \n* Release date: March 24, 2009\n* Label: Rounder Records\n|}\n\n===Music videos===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\"\n!
